Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Two Genealogical Traditions of Qahtan
Presentation of two genealogical opinions on Qahtan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly opinions on the genealogy of Qahtan and the chain of narrators supporting each.

Core Idea
Qahtan's ancestry: from Ismail or from Sam.

This passage examines the genealogical origins of Qahtan, the legendary ancestor of the Yemeni Arabs. Early Islamic genealogists presented two distinct lines tracing his descent—one linking him to the Ishmaelite line and the other to the Semitic line through Sam. Let's explore the traditions and the narrators who transmitted them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two opinions
Carefully read the Arabic text and translation. Notice that the passage begins with a tradition from Ibn Abbas stating Qahtan is from Ismail, then presents an alternative tradition tracing him to Sam.
Pay attention to the chain of narrators.
2
Note the correction about generations
The passage mentions that Ibn Abbas said there are thirty fathers between Qahtan and Ismail, but then notes that the correct number is three. Why might this correction be significant?
3
Reflect on the importance of genealogy
Consider why early scholars cared about Qahtan's lineage. How might this connect to broader debates about Arab identity and the descent of the Prophet?
This knowledge helps you see how genealogy served tribal and religious purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال شباب ونا هشام بن محمد بن السائب الكلبى قال حدثني ابي عن ابي صالح عن ابن عباس قال قحطان من ولد اسماعيل بن ابراهيم وبينه وبين اسماعيل ثلاثون أبا، قال وقال أبى لم يزل قحطان يعرفون ذلك وينتسبون اليه حتى كان زمن الحجاج، كذا قال والصواب ثلاثة آباء اخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الباقي بن محمد الانصاري ببغداد انا أبو محمد الحسن بن علی بن محمد الجوهرى انا أبو عمر محمد بن العباس بن حيوية الخزاز نا أبو الحسن بن معروف ابن بشر الخشاب نا الحسين بن محمد بن عبدالرحمن بن الفهم الفقيه نا محمد بن سعد كاتب الواقدى قال إلى قحطان جماع اليمن فمن نسبه إلى اسماعيل بن ابراهيم قال قحطان بن الهميسع بن تيم بن نبت بن اسماعیل ابن ابراهيم صلى الله عليهما، هكذا كان ينسبه هشام بن السائب الكلبي عن ابيه ويذكر عن أبيه أنه أدرك اهل النسب والعلم ينسبون قحطان إلى اسماعيل بن ابراهيم (۱) ومن نسبه إلى غير ذلك قال قحطان ابن فالغ بن عابر بن ارفخشد بن سام بن نوح صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن السمرقندى أنا أبو الحسين بن النقور انا محمد بن عبدالرحمن المخلص انا رضوان بن أحمد الصيدلاني نا أحمد ابن عبد الجبار العطاردی نا یونس بن بكير عن ابن اسحق قال ابراهیم بن آذر وهو في التوراة تارخ بن ناحور بن ارغو بن سارخ بن فالغ بن عابر بن شالخ این ارفخشذ بن سام بن نوح بن لمك بن متوشلخ بن خنوخ بن برد بن مهلاييل بن قمعان بن انوش بن شيث بن آدم ابى البشر عليه السلام وقال غیره قينان وقد اختلف في نسب ابراهيم عليه أفضل السلام وقول ابن اسحق مكتفى به عن قول غيره من علماء الإسلام.
Shabab said: Hisham ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sa'ib al-Kalbi narrated to us, he said: my father narrated to me from Abu Salih from Ibn Abbas, he said: Qahtan is from the descendants of Ismail ibn Ibrahim, and between him and Ismail there are thirty fathers. He said: And my father said: Qahtan had always been known and traced to that until the time of al-Hajjaj. Thus he said, but the correct is three fathers. We were informed by the shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi ibn Muhammad al-Ansari in Baghdad: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari informed us: Abu Umar Muhammad ibn al-Abbas ibn Hayawayh al-Khazzaz informed us: Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma'ruf ibn Bishr al-Khashshab informed us: al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Fahm al-Faqih informed us: Muhammad ibn Sa'd, scribe of al-Waqidi, said: The gathering place of Yemen is Qahtan. Whoever traces his lineage to Ismail ibn Ibrahim says: Qahtan ibn al-Humaysa' ibn Taym ibn Nabt ibn Ismail ibn Ibrahim, peace be upon them both. This is how Hisham ibn al-Sa'ib al-Kalbi traced him from his father, and he mentions from his father that he found the people of genealogy and knowledge tracing Qahtan to Ismail ibn Ibrahim. And whoever traces him otherwise says: Qahtan ibn Faligh ibn Abir ibn Arfakhshad ibn Sam ibn Nuh, peace be upon him. And we were informed by the shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi: Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Naqqur informed us: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Mukhlis informed us: Radwan ibn Ahmad al-Saydalani informed us: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Ataridi informed us: Yunus ibn Bukayr from Ibn Ishaq, he said: Ibrahim ibn Azar, and he is in the Torah Tarikh, ibn Nahur ibn Arghu ibn Sarukh ibn Faligh ibn Abir ibn Shalikh ibn Arfakhshad ibn Sam ibn Nuh, ibn Lamak ibn Mattushalikh ibn Khanukh ibn Bardi? ibn Mahlayil ibn Qaynan ibn Anush ibn Shith ibn Adam, the father of mankind, peace be upon him. And others said: Qaynan. And there is disagreement concerning the lineage of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, and the statement of Ibn Ishaq is sufficient over the statement of others among the scholars of Islam.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a detailed genealogical discussion concerning the origins of Qahtan and the lineage of Prophet Ibrahim. It begins with a tradition from Ibn Abbas stating that Qahtan is descended from Ismail with thirty generations between them. However, a correction is noted that the correct number is three generations. Then a chain of narrators leads to Muhammad ibn Sa'd who reports that Qahtan is the ancestor of Yemen, and two opinions are presented: one tracing him to Ismail (via al-Humaysa' etc.) and another tracing him to Sam (via Faligh etc.). The passage then provides the full lineage of Ibrahim as recorded by Ibn Ishaq, from Ibrahim back to Adam, with a note that others place Qaynan in the chain. The author concludes that Ibn Ishaq's version is sufficient. The passage serves to document scholarly differences in genealogy and to support the view that Qahtan is from Ismail, which was the position of early scholars.

Key Terms
قحطان
اسماعيل
هشام الكلبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the primary dispute is about Ibrahim's lineage, but the passage focuses on Qahtan's descent from Ismail versus Sam.
Correction: The passage is specifically about Qahtan's genealogy, not Ibrahim's.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abbas, how many fathers are between Qahtan and Ismail?
A) Thirty
B) Three
C) Forty
D) Fifteen

Key Takeaway
Scholars debated whether Qahtan descended from Ismail or from Sam, reflecting different tribal and religious affiliations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear conflicting claims about your own history—whether about your family, your community, or your faith—do you investigate the sources, or accept whichever story you prefer? This lesson shows scholars tracing chains with care. How thorough are you in seeking truth?
?
The author corrected a number from thirty to three. Are there beliefs you hold that might require similar correction? What would it take for you to admit that you were wrong?
?
Do you pride yourself on a particular ancestry or background? Reflect: In the sight of Allah, is that pride justified, or is it a distraction from what really matters?

The Lineage of Prophet Ibrahim (AS)
Presentation of Ibrahim's lineage from Ibn Ishaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the genealogy of Prophet Ibrahim as transmitted by Ibn Ishaq, from Ibrahim back to Adam, and note the scholarly consensus on its sufficiency.

Core Idea
Ibrahim's lineage is traced through Sam to Adam, with Ibn Ishaq's version deemed sufficient.

This passage presents the full lineage of Prophet Ibrahim as recorded by the renowned early historian Ibn Ishaq. It traces Ibrahim's ancestry through a chain of patriarchs back to Adam. Despite some variant readings, the author considers Ibn Ishaq's account to be authoritative for Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the genealogical chain
Carefully read the Arabic text and translation. Follow the names from Ibrahim back to Adam. Notice the variant name 'Tarikh' in the Torah.
This is a linear chain, so note each step.
2
Identify the variant
The passage mentions that some scholars place 'Qaynan' in the chain instead of another name. This shows there were minor differences.
3
Understand the author's stance
The author concludes that Ibn Ishaq's version is sufficient, implying that detailed genealogical disputes are not essential for faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال شباب ونا هشام بن محمد بن السائب الكلبى قال حدثني ابي عن ابي صالح عن ابن عباس قال قحطان من ولد اسماعيل بن ابراهيم وبينه وبين اسماعيل ثلاثون أبا، قال وقال أبى لم يزل قحطان يعرفون ذلك وينتسبون اليه حتى كان زمن الحجاج، كذا قال والصواب ثلاثة آباء اخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الباقي بن محمد الانصاري ببغداد انا أبو محمد الحسن بن علی بن محمد الجوهرى انا أبو عمر محمد بن العباس بن حيوية الخزاز نا أبو الحسن بن معروف ابن بشر الخشاب نا الحسين بن محمد بن عبدالرحمن بن الفهم الفقيه نا محمد بن سعد كاتب الواقدى قال إلى قحطان جماع اليمن فمن نسبه إلى اسماعيل بن ابراهيم قال قحطان بن الهميسع بن تيم بن نبت بن اسماعیل ابن ابراهيم صلى الله عليهما، هكذا كان ينسبه هشام بن السائب الكلبي عن ابيه ويذكر عن أبيه أنه أدرك اهل النسب والعلم ينسبون قحطان إلى اسماعيل بن ابراهيم (۱) ومن نسبه إلى غير ذلك قال قحطان ابن فالغ بن عابر بن ارفخشد بن سام بن نوح صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن السمرقندى أنا أبو الحسين بن النقور انا محمد بن عبدالرحمن المخلص انا رضوان بن أحمد الصيدلاني نا أحمد ابن عبد الجبار العطاردی نا یونس بن بكير عن ابن اسحق قال ابراهیم بن آذر وهو في التوراة تارخ بن ناحور بن ارغو بن سارخ بن فالغ بن عابر بن شالخ این ارفخشذ بن سام بن نوح بن لمك بن متوشلخ بن خنوخ بن برد بن مهلاييل بن قمعان بن انوش بن شيث بن آدم ابى البشر عليه السلام وقال غیره قينان وقد اختلف في نسب ابراهيم عليه أفضل السلام وقول ابن اسحق مكتفى به عن قول غيره من علماء الإسلام.
Shabab said: Hisham ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sa'ib al-Kalbi narrated to us, he said: my father narrated to me from Abu Salih from Ibn Abbas, he said: Qahtan is from the descendants of Ismail ibn Ibrahim, and between him and Ismail there are thirty fathers. He said: And my father said: Qahtan had always been known and traced to that until the time of al-Hajjaj. Thus he said, but the correct is three fathers. We were informed by the shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi ibn Muhammad al-Ansari in Baghdad: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari informed us: Abu Umar Muhammad ibn al-Abbas ibn Hayawayh al-Khazzaz informed us: Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma'ruf ibn Bishr al-Khashshab informed us: al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Fahm al-Faqih informed us: Muhammad ibn Sa'd, scribe of al-Waqidi, said: The gathering place of Yemen is Qahtan. Whoever traces his lineage to Ismail ibn Ibrahim says: Qahtan ibn al-Humaysa' ibn Taym ibn Nabt ibn Ismail ibn Ibrahim, peace be upon them both. This is how Hisham ibn al-Sa'ib al-Kalbi traced him from his father, and he mentions from his father that he found the people of genealogy and knowledge tracing Qahtan to Ismail ibn Ibrahim. And whoever traces him otherwise says: Qahtan ibn Faligh ibn Abir ibn Arfakhshad ibn Sam ibn Nuh, peace be upon him. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author concludes that Ibn Ishaq's version is 'sufficient over the statement of others.' In your own faith journey, are you content with what is sufficient, or do you get lost in minor disagreements? What area of your belief needs this kind of settled certainty?
?
This lineage connects you to Adam. Do you feel the weight of being part of a chain that goes back to the first human? What does that lineage demand of you today in terms of responsibility and gratitude?
?
The passage notes a variant about Qaynan but moves on. Is there a small doubt or dispute in your heart that you keep revisiting instead of accepting a sound position and moving forward? What would it take for you to embrace sufficiency and act on conviction?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Al-Ash'ari's Dream and Conversion
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's dream and his shift from Mu'tazilism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's intellectual crisis and prophetic dream led him to abandon Mu'tazilism and embrace the Sunnah.

Core Idea
A prophetic dream turned al-Ash'ari from Mu'tazili leader to Sunni champion.

This passage recounts the spiritual turning point in al-Ash'ari's life. Having mastered Mu'tazili theology, he found his teachers unable to answer his questions. In a state of perplexity, he prayed and saw the Prophet in a dream, who commanded him to follow the Sunnah. This dream transformed his approach to theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the story. Then read the translation to understand the details.
Notice the chain of transmission at the beginning, which shows the reliability of the report.
2
Identify the crisis
Find where al-Ash'ari's intellectual crisis is described. Why was he perplexed?
He was deeply versed in Mu'tazili kalam but could not get satisfactory answers from his teachers.
3
Understand the dream's command
What did the Prophet command al-Ash'ari? How did he respond upon waking?
The Prophet said 'عليك بسنتي' (You must follow my Sunnah). Al-Ash'ari then compared kalam with Qur'an and hadith and affirmed the latter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما سبب رجوع ابي الحسن عما كان عليه وتبريه مما كان يدعو اليه فأخبرني الشيخ أبو المظفر أحمد بن أبي العباس الحسن بن محمد البسطامي الشعيرى ببسطام، قال أنا جدى لأمى الشيخ الزاهد أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد بن الحسين بن سهل السهلكي البسطامي قال سمعت محمد بن على بن الحسين الواعظ رحمه الله ، يقول سمعت أحمد بن الحسين المتكلم قال سمعت بعض أصحابنا يقول : ان الشيخ أبا الحسن الله لما تبحر في كلام الاعتزال وبلغ غاية كان يورد الأسئلة على استاذيه في الدرس ولا يجد فيها جوابا شافيا فتحير فى ذلك فحكى عنه انه قال : وقع في صدرى فى بعض الليالي شيء مما كنت فيه من العقائد فقمت وصليت ركعتين وسألت الله تعالى أن يهديني الطريق المستقيم ونمت فرأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فشكوت إليه بعض مابي من الأمر، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عليك بسنتي فــانـتـبـهـت وعارضت مسائل الكلام بما وجدت في القرآن والأخـبـار فـأثـبـتـه ونبذت ماسواه ورائى ظهريا، وذكر أبو القسم حجاج بن محمد الطرابلسي من أهل طرابلس المغرب قال سألت أبا بكر اسماعيل بن أبي محمد بن اسحق الازدي القيرواني المعروف بابن عزرة رحمه الله عن أبي الحسن الأشعرى الله فقلت له قيل لى عنه انه كان معتزليا وأنه لما رجع عن ذلك أبقى للمعتزلة نكتا لم ينقضها فقال لى : الأشعرى شيخنا وإمامنا ومن عليه معولنا قام على مذاهب المعتزلة اربعين سنة، وكان لهم إماما ثم غاب عن الناس في بيته خمسة عشر يوما فبعد ذلك خرج إلى الجامع فصعد المنبر وقال : معاشر الناس اني إنما تغيبت عنكم في هذه المدة لأني نظرت فتكافات عندى الأدلة ولم يترجح عندي حق على باطل ولا باطل على حق فاستهديت الله تبارك وتعالى فهداني إلى اعتقاد ما أودعته في كتبي هذه وانخلعت من جميع ما كنت أعتقده كما انخلعت من ثوبي هذا وانخلع من ثوب كان عليه ورمى به ودفع الكتب إلى الناس فمنها كتاب (اللمع وكتاب اظهر فيه عوار المعتزلة سماه بكتاب ( كشف الأسرار وهتك الأستار ) وغيرهما فلما قرأ تلك الكتب أهل الحديث والفقه من أهل السنة والجماعة أخذوا بما فيها وانتحلوه واعتقدوا تقدمه واتخذوه اماما حتى نسب مذهبهم إليه قال لى أبو بكر فصار عند المعتزلة ككتابي أسلم وأظهر عوار ماتركه فهو اعدى الخلق إلى أهل الذمة وكذلك الأشعرى أعدى الخلق إلى المعتزلة، فهم يشنعون عليه من الأشانيع وينسبون إليه الأباطيل، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن أبي العباس بن أبي محمد بن آدم قال
As for the reason for Abu al-Hasan's return from what he was upon and his disavowal of what he was calling to: The shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Ahmad ibn Abi al-Abbas al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Bistami al-Sha'iri in Bistam informed me, he said: My maternal grandfather, the ascetic shaykh Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Sahl al-Sahlaki al-Bistami informed me, he said: I heard Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Husayn al-Wa'iz, may Allah have mercy on him, say: I heard Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Mutakallim say: I heard some of our companions say: When shaykh Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) had become deeply versed in the speech of the Mu'tazila and reached the utmost, he would pose questions to his teachers in the lesson and find no satisfactory answer, so he became perplexed. It is reported from him that he said: 'One night there arose in my chest some of what I was upon of beliefs, so I stood and prayed two rak'ahs and asked Allah Almighty to guide me to the straight path, then I slept and saw the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in a dream. I complained to him about some of my affair, and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "You must follow my Sunnah." So I woke up and compared the issues of kalam with what I found in the Qur'an and the traditions, so I affirmed it and cast aside everything else behind my back.' And Abu al-Qasim Hajjaj ibn Muhammad al-Tarabulusi from Tarabulus al-Maghrib mentioned, he said: I asked Abu Bakr Isma'il ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Azdi al-Qayrawani, known as Ibn 'Izzah, may Allah have mercy on him, about Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him, and I said to him: It was told to me about him that he was a Mu'tazili and that when he retracted from that he left some subtle points for the Mu'tazila that he did not refute. So he said to me: 'Al-Ash'ari is our shaykh and our imam and upon him is our reliance. He adhered to the doctrines of the Mu'tazila for forty years, and he was their imam. Then he secluded himself from people in his house for fifteen days. After that he went out to the mosque and ascended the pulpit and said: "O people, I have been absent from you during this period because I examined and found the evidences to be equivalent; no truth outweighed falsehood nor falsehood outweighed truth in my view. So I sought guidance from Allah, Blessed and Exalted, and He guided me to the belief that I have recorded in these books of mine, and I have divested myself of all that I used to believe, just as I divest myself of this garment of mine." And he took off a garment he was wearing and threw it away, and he gave the books to the people, among them the book (al-Luma') and a book in which he exposed the flaws of the Mu'tazila, which he called (Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar) and others. When the people of hadith and fiqh from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah read those books, they adopted what was in them and chose them, and they believed in his precedence and took him as an imam, until their madhhab was attributed to him. Abu Bakr said to me: 'So he became with respect to the Mu'tazila like a Muslim who apostatizes and exposes the flaws of what he left; he is the most hostile of creation to the dhimmis? Similarly, al-Ash'ari is the most hostile of creation to the Mu'tazila. So they spread defamations about him and attribute falsehoods to him.' We were informed by the shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Abbas ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Adam, he said...
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a historical account of the conversion of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy. It provides two versions: the first is a personal story transmitted through a chain of ascetics and preachers, describing al-Ash'ari's intellectual crisis: after mastering Mu'tazili theology, he found his teachers unable to answer his questions. In distress, he prayed and had a dream of the Prophet, who commanded him to adhere to the Sunnah. Upon waking, he compared kalam issues with the Qur'an and hadith and accepted the truth of the latter, rejecting all else. The second version, from Abu Bakr Isma'il ibn 'Izzah, describes al-Ash'ari's public renunciation: he had been a Mu'tazili leader for forty years, then secluded himself for fifteen days, after which he ascended the minbar, declared his abandonment of Mu'tazilism, and threw off a garment symbolizing his old beliefs. He then distributed his new works, such as al-Luma' and Kashf al-Asrar, which exposed Mu'tazili errors. The Ahl al-Sunnah accepted him as an imam. The passage also notes that al-Ash'ari became the most hostile opponent of the Mu'tazila, who in turn spread false accusations against him. The passage serves to authenticate al-Ash'ari's sincerity and to defend him against claims that he left unresolved points for the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a deep intellectual or spiritual crisis, do you turn to Allah with sincere prayer as al-Ash'ari did, or do you rely solely on your own reasoning? What step must you take tonight to seek divine guidance in a matter troubling your heart?
?
The Prophet told al-Ash'ari, 'You must follow my Sunnah.' Is there an area of your life where you have prioritized your own opinion, cultural habit, or intellectual trend over the clear Sunnah? Will you commit to comparing your views with the Qur'an and hadith and casting aside whatever contradicts them, no matter how attached you are?
?
Al-Ash'ari was a master of Mu'tazili theology, yet he had the humility to admit his perplexity and seek truth. What is the one belief or practice you hold most confidently that you have never truly questioned before Allah? Are you willing to ask Him tonight to guide you to the straight path, even if it means abandoning what you have built your identity upon?

Al-Ash'ari's Public Renunciation of Mu'tazilism
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's public renunciation and its aftermath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the public manner in which al-Ash'ari renounced Mu'tazilism and the impact of his conversion on the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's public renunciation and his books sealed his break with Mu'tazilism.

This passage provides a detailed account of al-Ash'ari's public conversion after forty years as a Mu'tazili leader. He secluded himself for fifteen days, then ascended the minbar and declared his new beliefs, throwing off a garment as a symbol. He distributed his new books, which refuted Mu'tazili positions, leading the Ahl al-Sunnah to embrace him as an imam and making him a target of Mu'tazili defamation.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of his public declaration
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the chain of transmission and the narrator's authority.
The narrator is Abu Bakr Isma'il ibn 'Izzah, a reliable scholar.
2
Observe the symbolic act
Notice al-Ash'ari's gesture of removing his garment. What does it symbolize?
He said 'I divest myself of all that I used to believe, just as I divest myself of this garment.'
3
Understand the reactions
How did Ahl al-Sunnah and the Mu'tazila respond to his conversion?
Ahl al-Sunnah accepted him and his books; the Mu'tazila hated him and spread false accusations.

And he took off a garment he was wearing and threw it away, and he gave the books to the people, among them the book (al-Luma') and a book in which he exposed the flaws of the Mu'tazila, which he called (Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar) and others. When the people of hadith and fiqh from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah read those books, they adopted what was in them and chose them, and they believed in his precedence and took him as an imam, until their madhhab was attributed to him. Abu Bakr said to me: 'So he became with respect to the Mu'tazila like a Muslim who apostatizes and exposes the flaws of what he left; he is the most hostile of creation to the dhimmis? Similarly, al-Ash'ari is the most hostile of creation to the Mu'tazila. So they spread defamations about him and attribute falsehoods to him.' Al-Ash'ari's Dream and Turn to Sunnah
A narration of al-Ash'ari's dream of the Prophet and his turn to Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Imam al-Ash'ari's transformative dream that led him from Mu'tazili kalam to Sunni orthodoxy, and the principle of prioritizing Qur'an and Sunnah over speculative theology.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s command to follow the Sunnah redirected al-Ash'ari’s entire theological method.

This passage recounts a pivotal moment in Islamic intellectual history: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's dream of the Prophet Muhammad. After years of mastering Mu'tazili dialectics, he found himself perplexed by unresolved questions. In a night of prayer and supplication, he received direct guidance from the Prophet himself, commanding him to adhere to the Sunnah. This event marked his turn from pure rationalism to a theology grounded in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the sequence of events.
Notice the chain of narration starting with 'سمعت أحمد بن الحسين المتكلم'.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's initial state
The passage describes al-Ash'ari as deeply learned in Mu'tazili kalam but unable to find satisfactory answers from his teachers, leading to perplexity.
This sets the stage for his need for guidance.
3
Observe the dream event
Al-Ash'ari prays two rak'ahs, asks for guidance, sleeps, and sees the Prophet in a dream. The Prophet commands him: 'You must follow my Sunnah.'
Dreams of the Prophet are considered truthful in Islamic tradition.
4
Note the outcome
Upon waking, al-Ash'ari compares the issues of kalam with the Qur'an and hadith, affirms the revealed texts, and discards everything else.
This shows his method: revelation as the criterion.
5
Reflect on the significance
Al-Ash'ari did not abandon kalam entirely but reformed its foundation by making it subservient to revelation. This episode marks the birth of Ash'ari theology.
This corrects the misconception that he rejected kalam outright.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقول سمعت أحمد بن الحسين المتكلم قال سمعت بعض أصحابنا يقول : ان الشيخ أبا الحسن الله لما تبحر في كلام الاعتزال وبلغ غاية كان يورد الأسئلة على استاذيه في الدرس ولا يجد فيها جوابا شافيا فتحير فى ذلك فحكى عنه انه قال : وقع في صدرى فى بعض الليالي شيء مما كنت فيه من العقائد فقمت وصليت ركعتين وسألت الله تعالى أن يهديني الطريق المستقيم ونمت فرأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فشكوت إليه بعض مابي من الأمر، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عليك بسنتي فـانـتـبـهـت وعارضت مسائل الكلام بما وجدت في القرآن والأخـبـار فـأثـبـتـه ونبذت ماسواه ورائى ظهريا
He said: I heard Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Mutakallim say: I heard some of our companions say: Indeed, Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari — may Allah have mercy on him — when he became deeply learned in the speech of the Mu'tazila and reached the utmost, he would pose questions to his two teachers in the lesson and not find a satisfactory answer from them, so he became perplexed about that. It is narrated from him that he said: Something of what I was in regarding beliefs fell into my chest one night, so I stood and prayed two rak'ahs and asked Allah Almighty to guide me to the straight path, and I slept. Then I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in a dream, and I complained to him about some of the matter I was in. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'You must follow my Sunnah.' Then I woke up and compared the issues of kalam with what I found in the Qur'an and the reports, so I affirmed it and cast aside everything else behind my back.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote about Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's conversion from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy. It begins by describing his deep immersion in Mu'tazili theology to the point where he would challenge his teachers with questions they could not answer, leaving him perplexed. The narrative then relates his personal account: one night, troubled by his beliefs, he performed supererogatory prayer, supplicated for guidance, and slept. In a dream, he saw the Prophet Muhammad, who commanded him to adhere to his Sunnah. Upon waking, he cross-examined the doctrines of kalam with the Qur'an and hadith, ultimately affirming the truth of the revealed texts and discarding all contrary opinions. The story emphasizes that his return was not a rejection of kalam per se, but a correction of method: he used the Qur'an and Sunnah as the criterion to judge theological positions.

?

?
The Prophet's command was simple and direct: 'You must follow my Sunnah.' In what area of your life—whether in worship, character, or daily decisions—are you following something other than the Sunnah? What would change if you took that command as literally and personally as al-Ash'ari did?

Al-Ash'ari's Forty Years as Mu'tazili and Public Repentance
A narration of al-Ash'ari's forty-year Mu'tazili tenure, seclusion, and public renunciation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical account of Imam al-Ash'ari's conversion from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy, including the circumstances of his seclusion and public declaration.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's repentance was a complete transformation, symbolized by stripping a garment.

This passage narrates the pivotal moment in Islamic intellectual history when Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari publicly renounced Mu'tazilism. The account, transmitted by reliable scholars, describes his forty-year adherence to the Mu'tazili school, a period of deep reflection, and his dramatic public repentance. Reading this narrative will give you insight into how al-Ash'ari became the founder of the Ash'ari school and why his works were embraced by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation to understand the sequence of events. Note the chain of narration starting from al-Tarabulusi.
The passage is a direct quotation from a reliable authority.
2
Note the duration and authority
Pay attention that al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili leader for forty years. This establishes his deep familiarity with the school he later refuted.
3
Observe the repentance scene
Notice his seclusion for fifteen days, his sermon on the pulpit, and the symbolic act of removing his garment. This dramatic gesture underscores the completeness of his renunciation.
The garment removal is a physical metaphor for shedding false beliefs.
4
Reflect on the analogy with Ka'b al-Ahbar
The passage compares al-Ash'ari to Ka'b al-Ahbar, a Jewish convert who became a fierce defender of Islam. Understand why this analogy is used to show al-Ash'ari's effectiveness against the Mu'tazila.
The analogy explains why the Mu'tazila slander him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر أبو القسم حجاج بن محمد الطرابلسي من أهل طرابلس المغرب قال سألت أبا بكر اسماعيل بن أبي محمد بن اسحق الازدي القيرواني المعروف بابن عزرة رحمه الله عن أبي الحسن الأشعرى الله فقلت له قيل لى عنه انه كان معتزليا وأنه لما رجع عن ذلك أبقى للمعتزلة نكتا لم ينقضها فقال لى : الأشعرى شيخنا وإمامنا ومن عليه معولنا قام على مذاهب المعتزلة اربعين سنة، وكان لهم إماما ثم غاب عن الناس في بيته خمسة عشر يوما فبعد ذلك خرج إلى الجامع فصعد المنبر وقال : معاشر الناس اني إنما تغيبت عنكم في هذه المدة لأني نظرت فتكافات عندى الأدلة ولم يترجح عندي حق على باطل ولا باطل على حق فاستهديت الله تبارك وتعالى فهداني إلى اعتقاد ما أودعته في كتبي هذه وانخلعت من جميع ما كنت أعتقده كما انخلعت من ثوبي هذا وانخلع من ثوب كان عليه ورمى به ودفع الكتب إلى الناس فمنها كتاب (اللمع وكتاب اظهر فيه عوار المعتزلة سماه بكتاب ( كشف الأسرار وهتك الأستار ) وغيرهما فلما قرأ تلك الكتب أهل الحديث والفقه من أهل السنة والجماعة أخذوا بما فيها وانتحلوه واعتقدوا تقدمه واتخذوه اماما حتى نسب مذهبهم إليه قال لى أبو بكر فصار عند المعتزلة ككتابي أسلم وأظهر عوار ماتركه فهو اعدى الخلق إلى أهل الذمة وكذلك الأشعرى أعدى الخلق إلى المعتزلة، فهم يشنعون عليه من الأشانيع وينسبون إليه الأباطيل
And Abu al-Qasim Hajjaj ibn Muhammad al-Tarabulusi, from the people of Tripoli in the Maghreb, mentioned: I asked Abu Bakr Isma'il ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Azdi al-Qayrawani, known as Ibn 'Azra — may Allah have mercy on him — about Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari — may Allah be pleased with him. I said to him: It was said to me about him that he was a Mu'tazili, and that when he recanted from that, he left some subtle points for the Mu'tazila that he did not refute. He said to me: Al-Ash'ari is our shaykh and our imam, and upon him is our reliance. He adhered to the schools of the Mu'tazila for forty years, and he was an imam for them. Then he disappeared from the people in his house for fifteen days. After that, he came out to the mosque, ascended the pulpit, and said: 'O people, I only absented myself from you during this period because I examined (the evidence) and the proofs were balanced for me; neither truth over falsehood nor falsehood over truth prevailed. So I sought guidance from Allah — blessed and exalted — and He guided me to the belief that I have deposited in these my books. And I have stripped myself of all that I used to believe as I strip myself of this garment of mine.' And he removed a garment that was on him and threw it away, and he distributed the books to the people. Among them are the book 'al-Luma' and a book in which he exposed the flaws of the Mu'tazila, which he named 'Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar' and others. When the people of hadith and fiqh from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah read those books, they accepted what was in them, adopted them, believed in his precedence, and took him as an imam, until his school was attributed to them. Abu Bakr said to me: So he became, with respect to the Mu'tazila, like Ka'b al-Ahbar who embraced Islam and exposed the flaws of what he had left; thus he is the most hostile of people to the People of the Book (dhimmis). Likewise, al-Ash'ari is the most hostile of people to the Mu'tazila. So they slander him with enormities and attribute falsehoods to him.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of al-Ash'ari's conversion, narrated by al-Tarabulusi from Ibn 'Azra. It first establishes al-Ash'ari's authority: he is our shaykh and imam. It then states that he was a Mu'tazili for forty years and their leader. He then secluded himself for fifteen days, after which he gave a public sermon. He explained his seclusion as a period of examination where proofs became balanced, so he sought divine guidance. Allah guided him to the belief recorded in his books. He dramatically removed a garment to symbolize his renunciation of his former beliefs, then distributed his new books: 'al-Luma' and 'Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar' (Revealing Secrets and Tearing Veils). The Ahl al-Sunnah accepted these books and made him their imam. The passage then draws an analogy with Ka'b al-Ahbar, a Jewish rabbi who converted to Islam and became its staunch defender. Just as Ka'b was most hostile to the Jews, al-Ash'ari is most hostile to the Mu'tazila, and hence they defame him.

Key Terms
الاعتزال
المنبر
اللمع
كشف الأسرار وهتك الأستار
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari recanted but left some subtle points unrefuted.
Correction: The narration states he wrote a book exposing their flaws and fully refuted them.

Checkpoint
How long did al-Ash'ari adhere to Mu'tazilism before his public repentance?
A) Twenty years
B) Fifteen days
C) Forty years
D) Thirty years

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's public repentance and full refutation of Mu'tazilism established him as the imam of Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari spent 15 days in seclusion, sincerely seeking guidance until Allah showed him the truth. When was the last time you isolated yourself from distractions to sincerely ask Allah for guidance on a matter of belief? What is stopping you from doing that today?
?
He physically stripped off his garment to symbolize renouncing his old beliefs. What false ideas or sinful habits are you still dressed in that you know contradict the truth? Will you strip them away and throw them aside, even if it feels humiliating?
?
After his conversion, al-Ash'ari became a fierce defender of the truth, even though it brought slander upon him. Are you willing to stand firmly for what you know is right, even if it means being mocked or rejected by those you once agreed with? Write one concrete step you will take this week to defend a truth of aqeedah.

Al-Ash'ari's Public Conversion
Narration of al-Ash'ari's public conversion with chain criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dramatic story of al-Ash'ari's public renunciation of Mu'tazilism in Basra and the critical assessment of its narration.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari publicly cut ties with his past, but the chain is weak.

This lesson presents a famous story of Imam al-Ash'ari's dramatic conversion from Mu'tazilism. After Friday prayer, he ascended the pulpit, cut a strap symbolizing his break, and declared his new Islam. However, the narrator is unknown, reminding us to be cautious with historical sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the dramatic actions: ascending the pulpit, cutting the strap, and the declaration.
The strap cutting is a symbolic act.
2
Understand the declaration
Al-Ash'ari says he was on a religion other than Islam and now embraces Islam. This implies he considered Mu'tazilism outside Islam.
This is a strong statement.
3
Assess the source
The text ends with 'al-Hamrani is unknown,' indicating a weak narrator. Consider how this affects the story's reliability.
Critical evaluation is key in historical studies.

The narrator adds a critical note that al-Hamrani himself is an unknown (majhul) narrator, indicating a weakness in the chain. The passage thus shows both the dramatic conversion story and a caveat about its reliability.

Al-Ash'ari's Three Dreams and the Prophetic Command to Defend Sunnah with Kalam
Three dreams guiding al-Ash'ari to defend the Sunnah with kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of prophetic guidance in al-Ash'ari's intellectual transformation and his reaffirmation of kalam in service of the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet commanded al-Ash'ari to defend the Sunnah using kalam, not abandon it.

This passage narrates the pivotal spiritual experience of Imam al-Ash'ari, whose three dreams in Ramadan reshaped his theological approach. The dreams show a gradual clarification: from a general command to uphold the narrated doctrines, to a specific directive to support them using kalam. This lesson traces that transformation and its implications for Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the full account of the three dreams, noting the progression and emotional states.
The text cuts off at the end of the third dream.
2
Identify the three dreams
Distinguish each dream: what the Prophet said, how al-Ash'ari reacted, and how the command changed.
3
Analyze al-Ash'ari's initial reaction
Notice his sorrow and his resolution to abandon kalam after the second dream, and the correction in the third.
4
Understand the final command
The Prophet explicitly says 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I only commanded you to support the doctrines narrated from me.' This is the key.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this story refutes the misunderstanding that al-Ash'ari rejected kalam entirely.

وذكر أبو عمرو عثمان بن أبي بكر ابن حمود بن أحمد السفاقسى المغربى وكان فهما فاضلا لبيبا عاقلا وقدم شيوخ شيوخنا أبو محمد عبدالعزيز بن أحمد الكتاني الحافظ وغيره قال سمعت الامام أبا عبد الله الحسين بن محمد يقول سمعت غير واحد من أئمتنا يحكى كيف كان بدء رجوع الامام المبرأ من الزيغ والتضليل أبي الحسن على بن اسماعيل أنه قال : بينا أنا نائم في العشر الأول من شهر رمضان رأيت المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا على المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فلما استيقظت دخل على أمر عظيم ولم أزل مفكر امهموما لرؤياى ولما انا عليه من إيضاح الأدلة في خلاف كان العشر الأوسط فرأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فقال لى ما فعلت فيما امرتك به فقلت يارسول الله وما عسى أن أفعل وقد خرجت للمذاهب المروية عنك وجوها يحتملها الكلام واتبعت الأدلة الصحيحة التى يجوز إطلاقها على الباري عز وجل قال لى انصر المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فاستيقظت وأنا شديد الأسف والحزن فأجمعت على ترك الكلام واتبعت الحديث وتلاوة القرآن فلما كانت ليلة سبع وعشرين وفي عادتنا بالبصرة أن يجتمع القراء وأهل العلم والفضل فيختمون القرآن في تلك الليلة مكثت فيهم على ماجرت عادتنا فأخذني من النعاس مالم أتمالك معه أن قمت فلما وصلت إلى البيت نمت وبى من الأسف على ما فاتني من ختم تلك الليلة أمر عظیم فرأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لى ماصنعت فيما امرتك به فقلت قد تركت الكلام ولزمت كتاب الله وسنتك فقال لى أنا ما أمرتك بترك الكلام إنما أمرتك بنصرة المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فقلت يارسول الله كيف ادع مذهبا تصورت مسائله وعرفت أدلته منذ ثلاثين سنة لرؤيا فقال لى لولا أني أعلم إن الله تعالى
And Abu 'Amr Uthman ibn Abi Bakr ibn Hammud ibn Ahmad al-Safaqsi al-Maghribi — and he was intelligent, virtuous, sagacious, and rational — mentioned, and [also] the teacher of our teachers, Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Kattani al-Hafiz and others said: I heard the Imam Abu 'Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Muhammad say: I heard more than one of our imams narrate how the beginning of the return of the imam declared free from deviation and error, Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il, was. He said: While I was asleep in the first ten days of Ramadan, I saw the Chosen One, peace be upon him. He said: 'O 'Ali, the doctrines narrated from me — they are the truth.' When I woke up, a great matter came upon me, and I remained thinking and worried about my dream and about what I was in of clarifying proofs in the refutation... [incomplete] ...the middle ten days passed, and I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, in a dream. He said to me: 'What did you do with what I commanded you?' I said: 'O Messenger of God, what can I do? I have expressed for the doctrines narrated from you aspects that speech (kalam) can bear, and I have followed the sound proofs that may be attributed to the Exalted Creator.' He said to me: 'Support the doctrines narrated from me, for they are the truth.' I woke up in great sorrow and grief, so I resolved to abandon kalam and follow hadith and recitation of the Qur'an. Then when it was the night of the twenty-seventh — and our custom in Basra was that the reciters and people of knowledge and virtue would gather and complete (khatm) the Qur'an on that night — I stayed with them according to our custom. Sleep overcame me such that I could not control myself, so I left. When I reached home, I slept, and I was extremely grieved over missing the completion of that night. Then I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said to me: 'What have you done with what I commanded you?' I said: 'I have abandoned kalam and adhered to the Book of Allah and Your Sunnah.' He said to me: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I only commanded you to support the doctrines narrated from me, for they are the truth.' I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, how can I abandon a school (madhhab) whose issues I have conceptualized and whose proofs I have known for thirty years because of a dream?' He said to me: 'Were it not that I know that Allah the Exalted...'
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy first-person narration of al-Ash'ari's conversion through three dreams in Ramadan. It is introduced with a chain of transmission. The story: In the first ten days, the Prophet tells him that the doctrines narrated from him (i.e., the Sunnah) are the truth. Al-Ash'ari is troubled and spends the middle ten days thinking. In the second dream, the Prophet asks what he has done. Al-Ash'ari replies that he has expressed the doctrines in ways that kalam permits using sound proofs. The Prophet commands: 'Support the doctrines narrated from me.' Al-Ash'ari, feeling sorrow, resolves to abandon kalam altogether and instead follow hadith and Quran recitation. On the 27th night, during a khatm gathering, he falls asleep and has a third dream. The Prophet asks again. Al-Ash'ari says he has abandoned kalam and adheres to Quran and Sunnah. The Prophet corrects him: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I only commanded you to support the doctrines narrated from me.' Al-Ash'ari then objects that he has followed his school for thirty years based on evidence, so how can he give it up for a dream? The Prophet's reply is cut off, but likely continues that Allah knows his sincerity or will guide him. The key point: The Prophet explicitly instructs al-Ash'ari to continue engaging in kalam, but now in defense of Sunni doctrines, not Mu'tazilism. This refutes claims that al-Ash'ari completely abandoned theology.

Key Terms
الرؤيا
المذاهب المروية
الكلام
الحديث
القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was commanded by the Prophet to abandon kalam entirely.
Correction: The third dream explicitly states: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I only commanded you to support the doctrines narrated from me.' So the command was to use kalam in defense of the Sunnah.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Prophet affirmed the use of kalam for defending the transmitted doctrines, dispelling the notion that theology is inherently blameworthy.

Al-Ash'ari's Three Dreams: From Rationalist to Defender
Al-Ash'ari narrates three prophetic dreams commanding defense of transmitted traditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic dreams guided al-Ash'ari to repurpose kalam (rational theology) for defending transmitted traditions rather than abandoning reason altogether.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's dreams transformed him from a rationalist opponent to a defender of tradition through reason.

This passage recounts a pivotal moment in Islamic intellectual history: Imam al-Ash'ari's personal account of three dreams during Ramadan that led him to abandon Mu'tazilism. The Prophet himself appears and corrects al-Ash'ari's initial misunderstanding of how to defend the faith. This story illustrates that kalam (theology) is not rejected but repurposed for defending orthodox beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for flow, then the English translation. Notice the three distinct dreams and the progression of al-Ash'ari's response.
The passage is a first-person narrative from al-Ash'ari himself.
2
Identify each dream's command
In each dream, the Prophet gives a command. Note what the Prophet says and how al-Ash'ari reacts. Especially observe the third dream's correction.
The first two dreams are similar; the third clarifies the role of kalam.
3
Analyze the Prophet's correction
In the third dream, al-Ash'ari says he abandoned kalam, but the Prophet corrects him: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I commanded you to support the transmitted schools.' Reflect on the difference.
This is the key turning point.
4
Understand 'madad' (divine reinforcement)
The Prophet promises that God will send al-Ash'ari reinforcements (madad) to clarify the aspects of transmitted traditions. Notice how al-Ash'ari later experiences receiving knowledge he never encountered before.
This reinforces the legitimacy of his new approach.

وذكر أبو عمرو عثمان بن أبي بكر ابن حمود بن أحمد السفاقسى المغربى وكان فهما فاضلا لبيبا عاقلا وقدم شيوخ شيوخنا أبو محمد عبدالعزيز بن أحمد الكتاني الحافظ وغيره قال سمعت الامام أبا عبد الله الحسين بن محمد يقول سمعت غير واحد من أئمتنا يحكى كيف كان بدء رجوع الامام المبرأ من الزيغ والتضليل أبي الحسن على بن اسماعيل أنه قال : بينا أنا نائم في العشر الأول من شهر رمضان رأيت المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا على المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فلما استيقظت دخل على أمر عظيم ولم أزل مفكر امهموما لرؤياى ولما انا عليه من إيضاح الأدلة في خلاف كان العشر الأوسط فرأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فقال لى ما فعلت فيما امرتك به فقلت يارسول الله وما عسى أن أفعل وقد خرجت للمذاهب المروية عنك وجوها يحتملها الكلام واتبعت الأدلة الصحيحة التى يجوز إطلاقها على الباري عز وجل قال لى انصر المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فاستيقظت وأنا شديد الأسف والحزن فأجمعت على ترك الكلام واتبعت الحديث وتلاوة القرآن فلما كانت ليلة سبع وعشرين وفي عادتنا بالبصرة أن يجتمع القراء وأهل العلم والفضل فيختمون القرآن في تلك الليلة مكثت فيهم على ماجرت عادتنا فأخذني من النعاس مالم أتمالك معه أن قمت فلما وصلت إلى البيت نمت وبى من الأسف على ما فاتني من ختم تلك الليلة أمر عظیم فرأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لى ماصنعت فيما امرتك به فقلت قد تركت الكلام ولزمت كتاب الله وسنتك فقال لى أنا ما أمرتك بترك الكلام إنما أمرتك بنصرة المذاهب المروية عنى فإنها الحق فقلت يارسول الله كيف ادع مذهبا تصورت مسائله وعرفت أدلته منذ ثلاثين سنة لرؤيا فقال لى لولا أني أعلم إن الله تعالى ذلك حتى بن عنده لما قمت عنك حتى يمدك بمدد من أبين لك وجوهها وكأنك تعـد إتياني إليك هذا رؤيا أو رؤياى جبريل كانت رؤيا أنك لاتراني في هذا المعنى بعدها فجد فيه فإن الله سيمدك بمدد من عنده قال فاستيقظت وقلت ما بعد الحق إلا الضلال وأخذت في نصرة الأحاديث في الرؤية والشفاعة والنظر وغير ذلك فكان يأتيني شيء والله ما سمعته من خصم قط ولا رأيته في كتاب فعلمت ان ذلك من مدد الله تعالى الذي بشرني به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم
And Abu Amr Uthman ibn Abi Bakr ibn Hammud ibn Ahmad al-Safaqsi al-Maghribi mentioned, and he was understanding, virtuous, intelligent, wise, and presented before our shaykhs' shaykhs Abu Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Kattani al-Hafiz and others, he said: I heard the Imam Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Muhammad say: I heard more than one of our imams narrate how the beginning of the return of the Imam cleared from deviation and misguidance Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il was that he said: While I was asleep in the first ten days of Ramadan, I saw al-Mustafa (peace be upon him) and he said: 'O Ali, the transmitted schools (al-madhahib al-marwiyya) from me are the truth.' When I woke up, a great matter entered upon me, and I remained thinking and anxious about my dream and about what I was upon of clarifying proofs in opposition. Then the middle ten days came, and I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the dream and he said to me: 'What have you done with what I commanded you?' I said: 'O Messenger of God, what can I do? I have extracted for the transmitted schools from you aspects that speech can bear and followed the sound proofs that are permissible to apply to the Exalted Creator.' He said to me: 'Support the transmitted schools from me, for they are the truth.' I woke up extremely sorrowful and grieved, so I resolved to abandon kalam and follow hadith and recitation of the Qur'an. Then when it was the night of the twenty-seventh, and our custom in Basra was that the reciters and people of knowledge and virtue would gather and complete the Qur'an that night, I stayed with them according to our custom. Sleep overcame me so that I could not control myself and I stood up. When I reached the house, I slept, with great grief for what I missed of completing the Qur'an that night. Then I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he said to me: 'What have you done with what I commanded you?' I said: 'I have abandoned kalam and adhered to the Book of God and your Sunnah.' He said to me: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I only commanded you to support the transmitted schools from me, for they are the truth.' I said: 'O Messenger of God, how can I leave a madhhab whose issues I have conceptualized and whose proofs I have known for thirty years because of a dream?' He said to me: 'Were it not that I know that God Almighty [ذلك حتى بن عنده] I would not have stood from you until He sends you a reinforcement from Him to make clear to you its aspects, and as if you count my coming to you this as a dream or the dream of Gabriel was a dream that you will not see me after this in this meaning. So strive in it, for God will send you a reinforcement from Him.' He said: I woke up and said: 'There is nothing after truth but misguidance.' And I began to support the hadiths on vision (ru'ya), intercession (shafa'a), and the beatific vision (al-nazar) and other things. Then something would come to me that, by God, I had never heard from any opponent nor seen in any book, so I knew that it was from the reinforcement of God Almighty with which the Messenger of God had given me glad tidings.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a detailed first-person narration by al-Ash'ari himself, reported through a chain of trustworthy scholars. It describes three prophetic dreams during Ramadan that prompted his return from Mu'tazilism to the Sunni position. In the first dream (first ten days), the Prophet commands him to support the transmitted traditions (al-madhahib al-marwiyya). Al-Ash'ari wakes up anxious but continues his rational approach. In the second dream (middle ten days), the Prophet asks what he has done, and al-Ash'ari replies that he has used rational interpretations. The Prophet again commands support. In the third dream (night of 27th), after al-Ash'ari had decided to abandon kalam altogether, the Prophet corrects him: he did not forbid kalam but commanded its use in defense of transmitted traditions. Al-Ash'ari protests that he cannot abandon his thirty-year old madhhab based on a dream. The Prophet reassures him that God will send him reinforcements (madd) to clarify the arguments. Al-Ash'ari wakes up convinced and begins to defend the Sunni positions on ru'ya (seeing Allah), shafa'a (intercession), and other matters. He then experiences receiving insights he had never encountered before, confirming the promised divine reinforcement.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari completely abandoned rational theology (kalam) after his repentance.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly told al-Ash'ari: 'I did not command you to abandon kalam; I commanded you to support the transmitted schools.' Al-Ash'ari repurposed kalam to defend orthodoxy, not abandon reason.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet command al-Ash'ari in the third dream regarding kalam?
A) To abandon kalam completely.
B) To use kalam to support the transmitted traditions.
C) To only follow the Qur'an and hadith.
D) To remain a Mu'tazilite.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's dream experience taught him that kalam should serve, not oppose, transmitted traditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you receive a clear command from Allah through His Book or His Prophet, do you hesitate because it conflicts with long-held habits or intellectual comfort, as al-Ash'ari initially did? What would it take for you to immediately obey, even if it means upending years of your own thinking?
?
Al-Ash'ari's first reaction was to try to reconcile his old ways with the command, and only after repeated dreams did he fully submit. Where in your life have you been 'extracting aspects that speech can bear' to avoid full obedience? What command from Allah are you still negotiating with instead of simply obeying?
?
The Prophet promised al-Ash'ari divine reinforcement if he strived. What area of your faith practice have you neglected because you felt inadequate or unsupported? Will you trust the promise of madad and take the first step today?

Al-Ash'ari's Dream and the Issue of Ru'ya
Al-Ash'ari recounts his dream with the Prophet over ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's dream of the Prophet led to his conversion from Mu'tazilism, focusing on the issue of ru'ya (seeing Allah).

Core Idea
A dream can be a vehicle for intellectual conviction, not just spiritual consolation.

This passage is a first-person account from al-Ash'ari himself, transmitted through a chain that includes al-Baqillani's companion. It reveals the personal and intellectual struggle behind his famous conversion. The Prophet appears in a dream and challenges him on the very issue that divided Mu'tazilites and Sunnis: whether Allah will be seen in the Hereafter. Al-Ash'ari's response shows that his eventual affirmation was not blind faith but the result of re-examining rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation, paying attention to the dialogue between the Prophet and al-Ash'ari. Notice how the Prophet addresses al-Ash'ari's intellectual objections.
2
Identify the turning point
Observe what makes al-Ash'ari change his position: the Prophet's command to re-examine the 'proofs of the intellect' as proofs, not doubts. This is the key moment.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this account tells us about the relationship between reason and revelation in Sunni theology. Why is this story significant for us today?

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقرأت فيما رواه الشيخ الزاهد أبو محمد عبدالقادر محمد الصدفي القيرواني المعروف بابن الخياط قال انا الشيخ الفقيه أبو بكر عبد الله بن محمد القرشي القيروانى قال نا أبو عبد الله الحسين بن عبد الله بن حاتم الازدى صاحب القاضي الجليل ابی بکر بن الباقلانی، قال كان الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل الأشعري رضوان الله عـلـيـه فـي الأصل معتزليا فحكى لنا أبو عبد الله الحسين المتكلم الرازي قال انا أبو الحسن بن مهدي بطبرستان قال حكى لنا الشيخ أبو الحسن رضى الله عنه قال كان الداعي إلى رجوعي عن الاعتزال وإلى النظر في أدلتهم واستخراج فسادهم أني رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في منامي في أول شهر رمضان فقال لى يا ابا الحسن كتبت الحديث؟ فقلت بلى يارسول الله فقال ما كتبت ان الله تعالى يرى في الآخرة فقلت بلى يارسول الله فقال لى صلى الله عليه وسلم فما الذى يمنعك من القول به؟ قلت أدلة العقول منعتنى فتأولت الأخبار، فقال لى وما قامت ادلة العقول عندك على أن الله تعالى يرى في الآخرة فقلت بلى يارسول الله فانما هی شبه فقال لي تأملها صلی أدلة، وغاب عنى الله وانظر فيها نظرا مستوفى فلیست بشبه بل هی عليه وسلم قال أبو الحسن فلما انتهيت فزعت فزعا شديدا وأخذت أتأمل ماقاله صلی الله عليه وسلم واستثبت فوجدت الأمر كما قال فقويت أدلة الإثبات فى قلبى وضعفت أدلة النفى فسكت ولم أظهر للناس شيئا وكنت متحيرا في أمرى فلما دخلنا في العشر الثانى من رمضان رأيته صلى الله عليه وسلم قد أقبل فقال يا ابا الحسن اى شيء عملت فيما قلت لك ؟ فقلت يارسول الله الأمر كما قلت صلى الله عليك والقوة في جانب الأثبات فقال لى تأمل سائر المسائل وتذكر فيها فانتبهت فقمت وجمعت جميع ما
And I read in what was narrated by the ascetic shaykh Abu Muhammad Abd al-Qadir Muhammad al-Sadafi al-Qayrawani known as Ibn al-Khayyat, he said: the jurist shaykh Abu Bakr Abd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Qurashi al-Qayrawani informed us, he said: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Abd Allah ibn Hatim al-Azdi, the companion of the noble judge Abu Bakr ibn al-Baqillani, narrated to us, he said: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari (may God be pleased with him) was originally a Mu'tazilite, so Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn al-Mutakallim al-Razi narrated to us, he said: Abu al-Hasan ibn Mahdi in Tabaristan informed us, he said: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan (may God be pleased with him) narrated to us, he said: The cause of my return from I'tizal and my examination of their proofs and extraction of their corruption was that I saw the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) in my dream in the first of Ramadan, and he said to me: 'O Abu al-Hasan, have you written the hadith?' I said: 'Yes, O Messenger of God.' He said: 'What have you written? That God Almighty is seen in the Hereafter?' I said: 'Yes, O Messenger of God.' He said to me (peace be upon him): 'Then what prevents you from saying it?' I said: 'The proofs of the intellect prevented me, so I interpreted the reports (ta'wil).' He said to me: 'And did not the proofs of the intellect establish for you that God Almighty is seen in the Hereafter?' I said: 'Yes, O Messenger of God, but they are doubts.' He said to me: 'Examine them [صلى أدلة، وغاب عنى الله] and look into them thoroughly, for they are not doubts, but they are proofs.' Abu al-Hasan said: When I finished, I became extremely terrified, and I began to examine what he (peace be upon him) said and verify, and I found the matter as he said. So the proofs of affirmation (ithbat) grew strong in my heart, and the proofs of negation weakened. So I remained silent and did not show anything to the people, and I was perplexed in my affair. When we entered the second ten days of Ramadan, I saw him (peace be upon him) approaching, and he said: 'O Abu al-Hasan, what have you done with what I said to you?' I said: 'O Messenger of God, the matter is as you said, may God bless you, and the strength is on the side of the affirmers.' He said to me: 'Examine the rest of the issues and reflect on them.' Then I awoke and stood up and gathered all that...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is another first-person account from al-Ash'ari, transmitted through a different chain that includes al-Baqillani's companion. It focuses specifically on the issue of ru'ya (seeing Allah in the Hereafter), which was a key point of contention between Mu'tazilites and Sunnis. In the dream, the Prophet asks al-Ash'ari why he does not affirm the vision of Allah despite having written the hadiths that state it. Al-Ash'ari admits that intellectual proofs prevented him and led him to interpret the texts figuratively (ta'wil). The Prophet then challenges him: did the intellectual proofs not establish that God is seen? Al-Ash'ari concedes they did, but considered them mere doubts. The Prophet commands him to examine them thoroughly, declaring they are proofs. After waking, al-Ash'ari verifies and finds the truth, so the arguments for affirmation strengthen in his heart while those for negation weaken. He remains silent initially, then in a second dream (second ten days), the Prophet instructs him to examine the rest of the issues. Al-Ash'ari then begins to gather all the points. This account highlights that al-Ash'ari's conversion was deeply intellectual and faith-based, and that the issue of ru'ya was pivotal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's conversion was purely emotional or based on a dream without rational basis.
Correction: The account shows he was commanded to re-examine rational proofs, and he did so, leading to intellectual conviction.

Checkpoint
What was the specific theological issue that the Prophet questioned al-Ash'ari about in the first dream?
A) The attribute of speech.
B) The beatific vision (ru'ya).
C) Intercession.
D) Predestination.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's conversion was driven by a dream that prompted a rigorous re-examination of rational proofs, leading him to affirm the beatific vision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find that your intellectual objections to a clear religious teaching are actually just doubts, will you stubbornly hold on to your reasoning, or will you submit to the Prophet's command as al-Ash'ari did? What is the one teaching you have been avoiding accepting?
?
Have you ever had a spiritual experience—like a dream, a prayer answered, or a sudden insight—that challenged your previous assumptions? Did you dismiss it or investigate it thoroughly like al-Ash'ari did after his dream? What might you be missing by ignoring such experiences?
?
If the Prophet himself appeared to you tonight and asked why you reject a certain sunna or hadith, what would you say? Are your excuses truly rational proofs or just comfortable doubts? What will you re-examine before you go to sleep?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Al-Ash'ari's Dream Vision and Conversion
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's conversion through three prophetic dreams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari was guided through prophetic dreams to abandon Mu'tazilism and adopt the Sunni creed, and why he continued to engage in kalam for defense of the truth.

Core Idea
Prophetic dreams transformed al-Ash'ari from a Mu'tazili skeptic to a Sunni defender.

Imam al-Ash'ari began his career as a Mu'tazili, but a series of dreams of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) led him to re-examine his beliefs. This passage from Ibn Asakir narrates the conversion in al-Ash'ari's own words, showing how he moved from rational denial to affirmation of the Sunni position on seeing Allah in the Hereafter, and how the Prophet himself commanded him to engage in kalam for the sake of truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of the first dream
Notice how the Prophet questions al-Ash'ari about the hadith on seeing Allah, and how al-Ash'ari admits he was prevented by rational proofs.
The hadith affirms the vision of Allah in the afterlife, a key Sunni belief.
2
Reflect on al-Ash'ari's response after waking
Observe how he investigates and finds the proofs of affirmation stronger, but remains silent.
3
Examine the second and third dreams
See the Prophet's persistent command to reflect and then to write, and al-Ash'ari's shift from abandoning kalam to embracing it.
The third dream is crucial: the Prophet commands him to write kalam, not abandon it.
4
Understand the lesson for us
Al-Ash'ari's story teaches that true adherence to Sunnah sometimes requires intellectual defense, not blind rejection of reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال كان الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل الأشعري رضوان الله عليه في الأصل معتزليا فحكى لنا أبو عبد الله الحسين المتكلم الرازي قال انا أبو الحسن بن مهدي بطبرستان قال حكى لنا الشيخ أبو الحسن رضى الله عنه قال كان الداعي إلى رجوعي عن الاعتزال وإلى النظر في أدلتهم واستخراج فسادهم أني رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في منامي في أول شهر رمضان فقال لي يا ابا الحسن كتبت الحديث؟ فقلت بلى يارسول الله فقال ما كتبت ان الله تعالى يرى في الآخرة فقلت بلى يارسول الله فقال لي صلى الله عليه وسلم فما الذي يمنعك من القول به؟ قلت أدلة العقول منعتنى فتأولت الأخبار، فقال لي وما قامت ادلة العقول عندك على أن الله تعالى يرى في الآخرة فقلت بلى يارسول الله فانما هي شبه فقال لي تأملها وغاب عني الله وصلى عليه وسلم قال أبو الحسن فلما انتهيت فزعت فزعا شديدا وأخذت أتأمل ما قاله صلى الله عليه وسلم واستثبت فوجدت الأمر كما قال فقويت أدلة الإثبات في قلبي وضعفت أدلة النفي فسكت ولم أظهر للناس شيئا وكنت متحيرا في أمري فلما دخلنا في العشر الثاني من رمضان رأيته صلى الله عليه وسلم قد أقبل فقال يا ابا الحسن اي شيء عملت فيما قلت لك؟ فقلت يارسول الله الأمر كما قلت صلى الله عليك والقوة في جانب الأثبات فقال لي تأمل سائر المسائل وتذكر فيها فانتبهت فقمت وجمعت جميع ما كان بين يدي من الكتب الكلاميات وضبرتها ورفعتها واشتغلت بكتب الحديث وتفسير القرآن والعلوم الشرعية، ومع هذا فإني كنت أتفكر في سائر المسائل لأمره صلى الله عليه وسلم إياي بذلك، قال فلما دخلنا في العشر الثالث رأيته ليلة القدر فقال لي وهو كالحردان ماعملت فيما قلت لك فقلت يارسول الله انا متفكر فيما قلت ولا أدع التفكر والبحث عليها إلا أني قد رفضت الكلام كله وأعرضت عنه واشتغلت بعلوم الشريعة، فقال لي مغضبا ومن الذي أمرك بذلك صنف وانظر هذه الطريقة التي أمرتك بها فإنها ديني وهو الحق الذي جئت به وانتبهت قال لي أبو الحسن فأخذت في التصانيف والنصرة واظهرت المذهب، فهذا سبب رجوعه عن مذاهب المعتزلة إلى مذاهب أهل السنة والجماعة رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه
He said: The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ismail al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, was originally a Mu'tazili. Abu Abdullah al-Husayn al-Mutakallim al-Razi narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Hasan ibn Mahdi in Tabaristan narrated to us, saying: The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan, may Allah be pleased with him, narrated to us, saying: What called me to return from Mu'tazilism and to examine their proofs and expose their corruption was that I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, in my dream in the first part of Ramadan. He said to me: O Abu al-Hasan, have you written the hadith? I said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Have you written that Allah the Exalted will be seen in the Hereafter? I said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah. He said to me, peace and blessings be upon him: So what prevents you from saying it? I said: The proofs of the intellect prevented me, so I interpreted the reports allegorically. He said to me: Did the proofs of the intellect not establish for you that Allah the Exalted will be seen in the Hereafter? I said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah, they are merely equivocal points. He said to me: Examine them, and he disappeared from me, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Abu al-Hasan said: When I awoke, I was terribly frightened and began to ponder what he, peace and blessings be upon him, had said, and I investigated and found the matter as he had said. So the proofs of affirmation strengthened in my heart and the proofs of negation weakened. I remained silent and did not reveal anything to people, and I was perplexed in my affair. Then when we entered the second ten days of Ramadan, I saw him, peace and blessings be upon him, approaching, and he said: O Abu al-Hasan, what have you done regarding what I told you? I said: O Messenger of Allah, the matter is as you said, may Allah bless you, and the strength is on the side of the affirmers. He said to me: Examine the other issues and reflect on them. Then I woke up, stood up, and gathered all the books of kalam that were before me, bundled them, and lifted them, and occupied myself with books of hadith, Quranic exegesis, and the religious sciences. Nevertheless, I continued to think about the other issues because of his command, peace and blessings be upon him, to me to do so. He said: When we entered the third ten days, I saw him on Laylat al-Qadr, and he said to me, appearing angry: What have you done regarding what I told you? I said: O Messenger of Allah, I am reflecting on what you said, and I do not cease reflection and research, except that I have abandoned kalam entirely and turned away from it and occupied myself with the sciences of the Sharia. He said to me angrily: And who commanded you to do that? Write and examine this path which I commanded you, for it is my religion and it is the truth I came with. And I awoke. Abu al-Hasan said: So I took up writing and supporting (the truth) and made the school public. This is the reason for his return from the schools of the Mu'tazila to the schools of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a first-person narrative by Imam al-Ash'ari recounting his conversion from Mu'tazilism to Sunni orthodoxy through a series of dreams of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Ibn Asakir prefaces the story with an isnad (chain of transmission). In the first dream, the Prophet asks al-Ash'ari if he has written that Allah will be seen in the Hereafter, a key Mu'tazili denial. Al-Ash'ari admits he has the hadith but was prevented by rational proofs, which he considered mere equivocations (shubah). The Prophet instructs him to examine them. After waking, al-Ash'ari investigates and finds the Sunni position stronger, but he remains silent. In the second dream, the Prophet asks what he has done; al-Ash'ari says the strength is with the affirmers. The Prophet tells him to reflect on other issues. Al-Ash'ari then abandons kalam books and takes up hadith, tafsir, and sharia sciences. In the third dream on Laylat al-Qadr, al-Ash'ari tells the Prophet he has abandoned kalam entirely, but the Prophet becomes angry and commands him to write and follow this path, declaring it his religion and the truth. Al-Ash'ari then openly adopts the Sunni school and begins writing in its defense. The passage concludes by stating that this was the cause of his return from Mu'tazilism to Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
رؤيا
الاعتزال
أهل السنة والجماعة
الرؤية
المتكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari completely rejected kalam after his conversion.
Correction: The Prophet himself commanded him to engage in kalam for defense of the truth, showing that kalam is acceptable when used to support Sunni beliefs.

Checkpoint

A) Abandon kalam and focus only on hadith
B) Continue writing kalam and support this path
C) Stay silent and not reveal his views
D) Return to Mu'tazilism

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's conversion was guided by prophetic dreams, leading him to affirm Sunni beliefs and defend them through kalam as commanded by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari was confronted with a truth he already knew but denied due to intellectual pride. What truth about Allah or His religion have you been avoiding because it challenges your own reasoning or comfort? Will you examine it today, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
?
The Prophet appeared angry when al-Ash'ari abandoned kalam entirely. Is there an area of Islamic knowledge or practice you have completely abandoned because of a previous bad experience or misunderstanding? How can you return to it with the right intention, seeking to support the truth?
?
Al-Ash'ari's conversion began with a dream that frightened him. Have you ever received a clear sign—through a dream, an ayah, or a life event—that called you to change, but you remained silent like al-Ash'ari initially did? What will it take for you to act on that sign now?

Al-Ash'ari's Dream and Return to Sunnism
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's dream and his return to Sunni creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's conversion from Mu'tazilism to Sunni Islam through a prophetic dream and its significance for the defense of Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
A dream on Laylat al-Qadr turned a leading Mu'tazili into a defender of Sunni Islam.

This passage narrates the pivotal moment when Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, after years of Mu'tazili scholarship, was redirected by a prophetic dream to champion Sunni orthodoxy. It highlights the power of sincere repentance and divine guidance, showing that even a deeply entrenched innovator can be guided back to the truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

Pay attention to the setting: the last ten nights of Ramadan, Laylat al-Qadr.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's initial state
Notice that al-Ash'ari had been deeply involved in kalam, then turned to hadith and Shari'a sciences, but still pondered theological questions due to the Prophet's earlier command.

In the dream, the Prophet confronts al-Ash'ari about abandoning kalam. The Prophet angrily commands him to compose and follow 'this way'—which he declares to be his religion and the truth.

Upon waking, al-Ash'ari immediately began composing works and defending the Sunni school. This marks his complete return from Mu'tazilism to Ahl al-Sunna.
5
Reflect on the lesson

This connects to the broader theme of Allah's mercy.

From the attributes? He who had in his hands the books of kalam, and I compiled them and raised them, and I occupied myself with books of hadith and Quran commentary and the legal sciences. Despite this, I used to ponder upon the various issues because of his (the Prophet's) command to me. He said: When we entered the third ten [nights], I saw him on Laylat al-Qadr. Commentary
This is a biographical passage that recounts the conversion of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari from Mu'tazilism to Sunni Islam. It begins by describing his earlier involvement with kalam books and his later shift to hadith, tafsir, and legal sciences. However, he continued pondering theological questions because the Prophet had commanded him to. During the last ten nights of Ramadan, on Laylat al-Qadr, he saw the Prophet in a dream. The Prophet asked why he had abandoned kalam. Al-Ash'ari replied that he was still thinking but had set aside kalam for the sciences of Sharia. The Prophet became angry, told him that no one commanded him to do that, and ordered him to write and promote the path he (the Prophet) had commanded, declaring it to be his religion and the truth. Al-Ash'ari awoke and began composing works and defending the Sunni school. The passage concludes by stating that this was the cause of his return from Mu'tazilism to Ahl al-Sunna.
