The Story of Abu Thawr: Leaving Bid'ah for the Proofs of al-Shafi'i
Ibn Asakir narrates how Abu Thawr and others left bid'ah after encountering al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the power of scriptural evidence, as demonstrated by Imam al-Shafi'i, can lead even those who initially opposed him to abandon their innovations and follow the truth.

Core Idea
Scriptural evidence can change hearts and minds, even moving enemies to become followers.

This lesson presents a remarkable historical account from the biography of Imam al-Shafi'i. It shows how two scholars who went to mock him were instead overwhelmed by his reliance on Quran and Hadith, leading them to abandon their previous positions. The story is a powerful testament to the strength of evidence-based discourse.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the chain of transmission and the key events.
The story is transmitted through a reliable chain, indicating its historical authenticity.
2
Identify characters and motives
Note that Husayn al-Karabisi, a proponent of ra'y, suggested mocking al-Shafi'i. Abu Thawr initially agreed. Understand their initial attitude.
They were from 'as'hab al-ra'y' (people of opinion) and viewed a hadith scholar as an opponent.
3
Reflect on the outcome
Notice how al-Shafi'i's consistent quoting of Allah and the Messenger caused the room to 'darken' (a metaphor for being overwhelmed). They left their bid'ah and followed him.
This shows that sincere engagement with evidence can lead to transformation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الأعز قراتكين بن الأسعد قال أنا الحسن بن على الجوهري أنا أبو الحسن علي بن عبدالعزيز بن مردك، أنا أبو محمد عبد الرحمن بن ابی حاتم الرازي قال أخبرني أبو عثمان الخوارزمى نزيل مكة فيما كتب إلى قال قال أبو ثور كنت انا واسحق بن راهويه وحسين الكرابيسي وذكر جماعة من العراقيين ماتركنا بدعتنا حتى رأينا الشافعي قال أبو عثمان وحدثنا أبو عبد الله الفسوي عن أبي ثور قال لما ورد الشافعى العراق جاءني حسين الكرابيسي وكان يختلف معى إلى أصحاب الرأى فقال قد ورد رجل من أصحاب الحديث يتفقه فقم بنا نسخر به، فقمت وذهبنا حتى دخلنا عليه فسأله الحسين عن مسألة فلم يزل الشافعي يقول : قال الله وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عليه وسلم حتى أظلم علينا البيت وتركنا بدعتنا واتبعناه.
And the Shaykh Abu al-A'azz Qaratakin ibn al-Asad informed us, saying: al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Jawhari related to us, saying: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abdul Aziz ibn Mardak related to us, saying: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim al-Razi related to us, saying: Abu Uthman al-Khwarizmi, resident of Mecca, informed me in a letter he wrote to me, saying: Abu Thawr said: I, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Husayn al-Karabisi, and he mentioned a group of Iraqis, did not leave our bid'ah until we saw al-Shafi'i. Abu Uthman said: And Abu Abdullah al-Fasawi narrated to us from Abu Thawr, saying: When al-Shafi'i came to Iraq, Husayn al-Karabisi came to me, and he used to go with me to the companions of opinion (ahl al-ra'y). He said: A man from the Companions of Hadith who is a faqih has arrived; get up so we can mock him. So I got up and we went until we entered upon him. al-Husayn asked a question, and al-Shafi'i kept saying: 'Allah said, and the Messenger of Allah said, peace be upon him,' until the room darkened upon us, and we left our bid'ah and followed him.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This is a historical narrative with a chain of transmission. It tells that Abu Thawr, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Husayn al-Karabisi, and others from the Iraqis did not leave their bid'ah until they saw al-Shafi'i. Then a specific story is related: when al-Shafi'i arrived in Iraq, Husayn al-Karabisi (who was a proponent of 'ra'y' or opinion-based jurisprudence) suggested to Abu Thawr that they go to mock the newcomer, who was a hadith scholar. They went and Husayn asked al-Shafi'i a question (likely to trip him up). However, al-Shafi'i kept responding by quoting from the Quran and the Sunnah of the Prophet, and his arguments were so overpowering that the room became dark (metaphorically, they were overwhelmed by the truth). As a result, they abandoned their bid'ah and followed al-Shafi'i. This story illustrates the power of scriptural proof in guiding people away from error.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that bid'ah cannot be overcome once a person is entrenched in it.
Correction: This story shows that even prominent scholars who held innovative views can abandon them when confronted with clear scriptural evidence, as seen with Abu Thawr and his companions.

Checkpoint

D) They decided to travel with him

Key Takeaway
The encounter with al-Shafi'i transformed the critics into followers because his answers were rooted in divine revelation, not human opinion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The room darkened upon them because the truth was so clear. Do you approach the Quran and Sunnah expecting to be humbled, or do you read them through the filter of your own assumptions? This week, choose one verse or hadith that challenges a comfort zone and meditate on it until it 'darkens' your room.
?
If someone came to mock al-Shafi'i, they left as followers. Is there someone you have dismissed as misguided whom Allah might use to guide you? Ask yourself: am I truly open to truth regardless of the vessel? Then make a concrete intention to seek truth from whoever possesses it, even if it means admitting you were wrong.

How Imam al-Shafi'i Turned Innovators Back to the Sunnah
Ibn Asakir narrates a story of scholars abandoning innovation after encountering Imam al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the example of Imam al-Shafi'i demonstrates that abandoning innovation for the Sunnah is praiseworthy and does not diminish one's previous status.

Core Idea
Returning from innovation to the Sunnah elevates, not diminishes.

Ibn Asakir presents a powerful historical example to show that even great scholars can abandon innovation without losing their rank. He begins with a general principle, supports it with the analogy of the Companions, and then narrates a specific incident involving Imam al-Shafi'i that changed the hearts of his contemporaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Let the story's flow come through before you interpret its deeper meaning.
Notice that the passage has two parts: a general statement and a specific narrative.
2
Identify the general principle
The passage begins by stating that imams who recanted from innovations were not diminished by their past. They returned to following (al-ittiba'). This sets the theme.
The principle is supported by the example of the Companions who left idol worship.
3
Analyze the story of al-Shafi'i
Focus on the chain of narrators and the story itself: three scholars who were following innovation came to mock al-Shafi'i, but his reliance on Quran and Sunnah overwhelmed them.
The phrase 'until the house became dark upon us' indicates their realization was profound.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider what this story teaches about repentance and returning to the Sunnah. Innovation can be abandoned, and that return is a virtue.
The scholars are not named as lesser for their past; rather, their turning is praised.

الأئمة كانوا على أشياء رجعوا عنها وتركوها بعد ما سلكوها وتبرأوا منها فلم ينقصهم ماكانوا عليه من الابتداع لما أقلعوا عنه ورجعوا إلى الاتباع وقد كان أكثر الصحابة الكرام يدينون بعبادة الأوثان والأصنام، ثم صاروا بعد سادة أهل الإسلام، وقادة المسلمين في الأمور العظام، وقد أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الأعز قراتكين بن الأسعد قال أنا الحسن بن على الجوهري أنا أبو الحسن علي بن عبدالعزيز بن مردك، أنا أبو محمد عبد الرحمن بن ابی حاتم الرازي قال أخبرني أبو عثمان الخوارزمى نزيل مكة فيما كتب إلى قال قال أبو ثور كنت انا واسحق بن راهويه وحسين الكرابيسي وذكر جماعة من العراقيين ما تركنا بدعتنا حتى رأينا الشافعي قال أبو عثمان وحدثنا أبو عبد الله الفسوي عن أبي ثور قال لما ورد الشافعى العراق جاءني حسين الكرابيسي وكان يختلف معى إلى أصحاب الرأى فقال قد ورد رجل من أصحاب الحديث يتفقه فقم بنا نسخر به، فقمت وذهبنا حتى دخلنا عليه فسأله الحسين عن مسألة فلم يزل الشافعي يقول : قال الله وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حتى أظلم علينا البيت وتركنا بدعتنا واتبعناه.
The imams were upon things that they recanted from and abandoned after they had traversed them and disavowed from them, so what they were upon of innovation did not diminish them when they desisted from it and returned to following. And most of the noble Companions used to practice worship of idols and statues, then they became afterwards the masters of the people of Islam and the leaders of the Muslims in great matters. And the Shaykh Abu al-A'azz Qaratkin ibn al-Asad informed us: he said: al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Jawhari told us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Murdak told us: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim al-Razi told us: he said: Abu Uthman al-Khwarizmi, a resident of Mecca, informed me in what he wrote to me: he said: Abu Thawr said: I, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and Husayn al-Karabisi, and he mentioned a group of Iraqis, we did not leave our innovation until we saw al-Shafi'i. Abu Uthman said: and Abu Abd Allah al-Fasawi narrated to us from Abu Thawr: he said: When al-Shafi'i came to Iraq, Husayn al-Karabisi came to me, and he used to go with me to the people of opinion, and he said: A man from the people of hadith who seeks fiqh has arrived; come, let us mock him. So I went and we went until we entered upon him. Then al-Husayn asked him about a matter, and al-Shafi'i kept saying: 'Allah said, and the Messenger of Allah said' until the house became dark upon us, and we left our innovation and followed him.

Commentary
This passage is a narrative argument demonstrating that earlier scholars who abandoned innovations were not diminished in status. Ibn Asakir begins with a general principle: the imams who recanted from their innovations and returned to following (al-ittiba') were not lessened by what they had previously adhered to. He then provides a powerful analogy: most of the noble Companions originally worshipped idols, yet after embracing Islam they became the masters and leaders of the Muslims. Then he reports a specific chain of transmission illustrating this principle. The story involves Abu Thawr, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and Husayn al-Karabisi, who were following some innovation (likely excessive reliance on opinion). When al-Shafi'i arrived in Iraq, Husayn suggested they mock him. They went to him, but when al-Shafi'i responded to a question by repeatedly citing the Qur'an and Sunnah, they were overwhelmed and abandoned their innovation, following him instead. The lesson is that returning from innovation to the Sunnah is praiseworthy and does not harm one's past; rather, it elevates one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Key Takeaway
Innovation once adopted can be abandoned, and that return is a sign of virtue, not weakness.

?

?

The Prophet's Glad Tidings of the Ash'aris' Arrival
Ibn Asakir presents multiple chains of a hadith praising the Ash'aris' arrival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses multiple chains of a hadith to establish the prophetic praise of the Ash'aris and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
The Prophet foretold the arrival of people with softer hearts—the Ash'aris.

Ibn Asakir begins the chapter by citing several versions of a hadith in which the Prophet announces that a people with softer hearts will come, and they turn out to be the Ash'aris led by Abu Musa. This lesson examines these narrations and their role in defending the Ash'ari school.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter heading
Notice how the heading connects the hadith to the knowledge of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, setting the purpose of the compilation.
2
Analyze the first narration from Anas
Identify the key phrase 'أرق أفئدة' (softer hearts) and the Ash'aris' chanting.
3
Compare the multiple chains
Observe that each chain transmits the same essential message, strengthening the hadith's authenticity.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask why Ibn Asakir includes so many chains—it is to provide overwhelming evidence for the virtue of the Ash'aris.

Source Text

باب ما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من بشارته بقدوم أبي موسى وأهل اليمن وإشارته إلى ما يظهر من علم أبي الحسن

أخبرنا أبو عبد الله بن أبي مسعود الصاعدي أنبأ أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الخسروجردي، أنبأ محمد بن عبدالله الحافظ، ثنا أبو العباس محمد ابن يعقوب ثنا محمد بن إسحاق ثنا عبد الله بن بكير ثنا حميد عن أنس قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ) يقدم عليكم قوم هم أرق أفئدة منكم ) فلما دنوا من المدينة جعلوا يرتجزون : ( غدا نلقى الأحبة محمدا وحزبه ) فقدم الأشعريون معهم أبو موسى

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن الحصين الشيباني ببغداد أنبأ أبو علي الحسن بن علي بن محمد التميمي أنبأ أبو بكر أحمد بن جعفر بن حمدان التنطيعي ثنا أبو عبد الرحمن عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل، حدثني أبي رحمه الله ثنا ابن أبي عدي عن حميد عن أنس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( يقدم عليكم أقوام هم أرق منكم قلوبا ) قال فقدم الأشعريون فيهم أبو موسى الأشعري فلما دنوا من المدينة كانوا يرتجزون يقولون ( غدا نلقى الأحبة محمدا وحزبه )

قال وثنا عبد الله بن أحمد قال ثنا أبي قال ثنا يحيى عن حميد ويزيد قال أنبأ حميد عن أنس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ) يقدم عليكم أقوام أرق منكم أفئدة) فقدم الأشعريون فيهم أبو موسى فجعلوا لما دنوا من المدينة يرتجزون ( غدا نلقى الأحبة محمدا وحزبه )

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر عبد المنعم بن عبد الكريم أنبأ أبو سعد محمد بن عبدالرحمن أنبأ أبو عمرو محمد بن أحمد بن حمدان وأخبرتنا الشريفة أم المجتبى فاطمة بنت ناصر بن الحسن الحسينية وأم البهاء فاطمة بنت محمد بن أحمد بن البغدادي بأصبهان قالتا أنبأ أبو القسم إبراهيم بن منصور سبط بحرويه أنبأ أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن المقري قال أنبأ أبو يعلى أحمد بن علي التميمي ثنا زهير بن حرب ثنا يزيد هو ابن هارون قال أنبأ وقال ابن حمدان ثنا حميد عن أنس رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( يقدم قوم هم أرق أفئدة منكم ) فقدم الأشعريون فيهم أبو موسى فجعلوا يرتجزون يقولون ( غدا نلقى الأحبة محمدا وحزبه )

رواه أبو عبد الرحمن النسائي في سننه عن ابن مثنى عن بن الحارث عن حميد

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل الفقيه أنبأ أبو بكر أحمد بن منصور بن خلف البزاز أنبأ أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الله محمد الشيباني الجوزقي أنبأ أبو حامد بن الشرقي ثنا محمد بن حيويه ثنا أبو اليمان أنبأ شعيب قال أنبأ أبو الزناد عن الأعرج عن أبي هريرة عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( أتاكم أهل اليمن هم أضعف قلوبا وأرق أفئدة، الإيمان يمان والحكمة يمانية ورأس الكفر نحو المشرق والفخر والخيلاء في الفدادين والخيلاء في أهل الخيل والإبل - الفدادين أهل الوبر - والسكينة في أهل الغنم

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله الحسين بن عبدالملك الخلال قال أنبأ أبو القسم إبراهيم بن منصور بن إبراهيم السلمي، أنبأ أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن علي بن المقري أنبأ أبو يعلى أحمد بن علي بن المثنى الموصلي ثنا أبو خيثمة ثنا جرير عن الأعمش عن أبي صالح عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( الإيمان يمان والحكمة يمانية أتاكم أهل اليمن هم أرق أفئدة وألين قلوبا )

أخرجه البخاري ومسلم في صحيحيهما فرواه مسلم عن أبي خيثمة

أخبرناه أبو بكر عبدالغفار بن محمد بن الحسين الشيروي في كتابه وحدثني أبو المحاسن عبد الرزاق بن محمد الطبسي بنيسابور عنه قال أنبأ القاضي أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسن بن أحمد الحيري واخبرناه أبو عبدالله محمد بن الفضل أنبأ أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين أنبأ أبو عبدالله الحافظ قالا ثنا أبو العباس محمد بن يعقوب ثنا أحمد بن عبد الجبار ثنا أبو معوية عن الأعمش عن أبي صالح عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( أتاكم أهل اليمن هم ألين قلوبا وأرق أفئدة الإيمان يمان والحكمة يمانية ) زاد الحيري قال أبو معوية أراه قال رأس الكفر قبل المشرق

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن الحسن بن علي بن إبراهيم المقري ببغداد ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو الحسن محمد بن علي بن محمد بن عبيد الله بن عبد الصمد بن المهتدي بالله أنبأ أبو الحسن علي بن عمر بن محمد بن الحسن بن شادان السكري الحربي قال ثنا أبو حبيب العباس بن أحمد بن
Chapter: What has been narrated from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, of his glad tidings of the arrival of Abu Musa and the people of Yemen, and his indication of what would appear of the knowledge of Abu al-Hasan.

We were informed by Abu Abdullah ibn Abi Mas'ud al-Sa'idi: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Khusrawjirdi told us: Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz told us: Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub told us: Muhammad ibn Ishaq told us: Abdullah ibn Bukayr told us: Humayd told us from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you a people who are softer in hearts than you.' When they drew near to Medina, they began to chant: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa.

We were informed by Sheikh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn al-Husayn al-Shaybani in Baghdad: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tamimi told us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Tanuti'i told us: Abu Abd al-Rahman Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal told us: My father, may God have mercy on him, told me: Ibn Abi Adi told us from Humayd from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you people who are softer than you in hearts.' He said: So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. When they drew near to Medina, they were chanting, saying: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

He said: And Abdullah ibn Ahmad told us: My father told us: Yahya told us from Humayd and Yazid who said: Humayd told us from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you people softer than you in hearts.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa. When they drew near to Medina, they began to chant: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu al-Muzaffar Abd al-Mun'im ibn Abd al-Karim: Abu Sa'd Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman told us: Abu Amr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hamdan told us, and the noble lady Umm al-Mujtaba Fatima bint Nasir ibn al-Hasan al-Husayniyya and Umm al-Baha Fatima bint Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Baghdadi in Isfahan both said: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur Sabt Bahruwayh told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Muqri' told us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali al-Tamimi told us: Zuhayr ibn Harb told us: Yazid ibn Harun told us: he said: and Ibn Hamdan said: Humayd told us from Anas, may God be pleased with him, that the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come a people who are softer in hearts than you.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa, and they began to chant, saying: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

It was narrated by Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Nasa'i in his Sunan from Ibn Muthanna from Ibn al-Harith from Humayd.

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Khalaf al-Bazzaz told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah Muhammad al-Shaybani al-Jawzaqi told us: Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi told us: Muhammad ibn Hayyuwayh told us: Abu al-Yaman told us: Shu'ayb told us: Abu al-Zinad told us from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayra from him that he said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the weakest in hearts and the softest in feeling. Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni. The head of disbelief is towards the east. Pride and arrogance are among the owners of camels, and arrogance among the owners of horses and camels - the owners of camels are the people of the desert - and tranquility is among the owners of sheep.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Abdullah al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik al-Khallal: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur ibn Ibrahim al-Sulami told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn al-Muqri' told us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Muthanna al-Mawsili told us: Abu Khaythama told us: Jarir told us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni. The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the softest in hearts and the tenderest in hearts.'

Al-Bukhari and Muslim both narrated it in their Sahihs. Muslim narrated it from Abu Khaythama.

We were informed by Abu Bakr Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirwi in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him: al-Qadi Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad al-Hayri told us, and we were informed by Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn told us: Abu Abdullah al-Hafiz told us: both said: Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub told us: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar told us: Abu Mu'awiya told us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the tenderest in hearts and the softest in feeling. Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni.' Al-Hayri added: Abu Mu'awiya said: I think he said: 'The head of disbelief is towards the east.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Muqri' in Baghdad: al-Qadi al-Sharif Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Abd al-Samad ibn al-Muhtadi Billah told us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Shadan al-Sukri al-Harbi told us: Abu Habib al-Abbas ibn Ahmad ibn
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of multiple hadith narrations (with various chains of transmission) from the Prophet Muhammad praising the people of Yemen, specifically the Ash'ari tribe and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The chapter title indicates the subject: 'Chapter on what has been narrated from the Prophet of his glad tidings of the arrival of Abu Musa and the people of Yemen, and his indication of what would appear of the knowledge of Abu al-Hasan' (referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school). Ibn Asakir is gathering these narrations as evidence for the virtue and precedence of the Ash'aris, which is part of his broader defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari against detractors.

The first narration is via Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet announces that a people with softer hearts will come, and when the Ash'aris arrive with Abu Musa, they recite a verse about meeting the beloved (Muhammad). This is repeated through several chains: from Anas via different narrators (Ibn Bukayr, Ibn Abi Adi, Yahya, Yazid, Humayd; via Zuhayr ibn Harb; via Ibn Hamdan). Then it is mentioned that al-Nasa'i also narrated it.

The second set of narrations comes from Abu Hurayra, with multiple chains: the Prophet says the people of Yemen have come, they are the weakest in hearts and softest in feeling, and he emphasizes that faith and wisdom are Yemeni, while the head of disbelief is towards the east, and pride is among camel owners. He also mentions tranquility among sheep owners. This hadith is reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. Then another version from Abu Hurayra via al-A'mash adds that they are the softest and tenderest in hearts.

A third version from Abu Hurayra via Abu Mu'awiya repeats the same content, with an addition that the head of disbelief is towards the east.

Throughout, Ibn Asakir meticulously cites his teachers and chains to authenticate these reports. The purpose is not just to record hadith but to establish a doctrinal point: the Ash'aris (descendants of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari) are divinely praised, and by extension, the theological school attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is rooted in this virtuous lineage. The core argument is that the Prophet's praise serves as a refutation of those who disparage the Ash'ari school.

Key Terms
أبو موسى الأشعري
الأشعريون
أرق أفئدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These hadith are only historical reports about a migration.
Correction: Ibn Asakir uses them to defend the Ash'ari school by showing prophetic praise of the Ash'aris.

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Asakir include multiple chains for the same hadith?
A) To show the different places where the hadith was narrated
B) To provide overwhelming evidence for the virtue of the Ash'aris
C) To compare the wording of different narrations
D) To fulfill a requirement of chapter length

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's praise of the Ash'aris is established through multiple chains, supporting the Ash'ari school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Prophet praised a group for having 'softer hearts,' do you see that quality in yourself? What specific steps can you take today to make your heart more tender and receptive to the truth?
?
The Ash'aris chanted with joy at the prospect of meeting the Prophet. Do you truly long to meet him, or have worldly distractions dulled that eagerness? What is one attachment you need to loosen to increase that longing?
?
Ibn Asakir preserved this hadith through multiple chains to defend a school of thought. Are you willing to seek out and preserve the truth with such diligence, even if it challenges your comfortable assumptions? What will you change in your study habits starting now?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Virtue of Yemen and the Ash'ari Connection
Ibn Asakir compiles hadith from Abu Hurayra praising Yemen and connecting it to faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about faith being Yemeni and wisdom being Yemeni connects to the praise of the Ash'aris and the refutation of their detractors.

Core Idea
The Prophet declared faith and wisdom to be Yemeni, highlighting the virtue of the Ash'aris.

Ibn Asakir now presents hadith from Abu Hurayra in which the Prophet describes the people of Yemen as soft-hearted and declares that faith and wisdom are Yemeni. This lesson explores these narrations and their significance for the Ash'ari school.

Guided Path
1
Read the Abu Hurayra narrations
Identify the phrases: 'الإيمان يمان والحكمة يمانية' and 'رأس الكفر قبل المشرق'.
2
Compare with the previous hadith
Notice the recurring theme of soft hearts and Yemeni origin.
3
Analyze the reference to the east
Understand that the Prophet locates disbelief towards the east, contrasting with Yemen's virtue.
4
Connect to the Ash'ari school
Ibn Asakir uses these hadith to link the Ash'aris to the praised Yemeni origin.

أخرجه البخاري ومسلم في صحيحيهما فرواه مسلم عن أبي خيثمة

أخبرناه أبو بكر عبدالغفار بن محمد بن الحسين الشيروي في كتابه وحدثني أبو المحاسن عبد الرزاق بن محمد الطبسي بنيسابور عنه قال أنبأ القاضي أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسن بن أحمد الحيري واخبرناه أبو عبدالله محمد بن الفضل أنبأ أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين أنبأ أبو عبدالله الحافظ قالا ثنا أبو العباس محمد بن يعقوب ثنا أحمد بن عبد الجبار ثنا أبو معوية عن الأعمش عن أبي صالح عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( أتاكم أهل اليمن هم ألين قلوبا وأرق أفئدة الإيمان يمان والحكمة يمانية ) زاد الحيري قال أبو معوية أراه قال رأس الكفر قبل المشرق

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن الحسن بن علي بن إبراهيم المقري ببغداد ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو الحسن محمد بن علي بن محمد بن عبيد الله بن عبد الصمد بن المهتدي بالله أنبأ أبو الحسن علي بن عمر بن محمد بن الحسن بن شادان السكري الحربي قال ثنا أبو حبيب العباس بن أحمد بن
Chapter: What has been narrated from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, of his glad tidings of the arrival of Abu Musa and the people of Yemen, and his indication of what would appear of the knowledge of Abu al-Hasan.

We were informed by Abu Abdullah ibn Abi Mas'ud al-Sa'idi: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Khusrawjirdi told us: Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz told us: Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub told us: Muhammad ibn Ishaq told us: Abdullah ibn Bukayr told us: Humayd told us from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you a people who are softer in hearts than you.' When they drew near to Medina, they began to chant: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa.

We were informed by Sheikh Abu al-Qasim Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn al-Husayn al-Shaybani in Baghdad: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tamimi told us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Tanuti'i told us: Abu Abd al-Rahman Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal told us: My father, may God have mercy on him, told me: Ibn Abi Adi told us from Humayd from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you people who are softer than you in hearts.' He said: So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. When they drew near to Medina, they were chanting, saying: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

He said: And Abdullah ibn Ahmad told us: My father told us: Yahya told us from Humayd and Yazid who said: Humayd told us from Anas who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come to you people softer than you in hearts.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa. When they drew near to Medina, they began to chant: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu al-Muzaffar Abd al-Mun'im ibn Abd al-Karim: Abu Sa'd Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman told us: Abu Amr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hamdan told us, and the noble lady Umm al-Mujtaba Fatima bint Nasir ibn al-Hasan al-Husayniyya and Umm al-Baha Fatima bint Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Baghdadi in Isfahan both said: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur Sabt Bahruwayh told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Muqri' told us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali al-Tamimi told us: Zuhayr ibn Harb told us: Yazid ibn Harun told us: he said: and Ibn Hamdan said: Humayd told us from Anas, may God be pleased with him, that the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'There will come a people who are softer in hearts than you.' So the Ash'aris came, among them Abu Musa, and they began to chant, saying: 'Tomorrow we will meet the beloved, Muhammad and his party.'

It was narrated by Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Nasa'i in his Sunan from Ibn Muthanna from Ibn al-Harith from Humayd.

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Faqih: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Khalaf al-Bazzaz told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah Muhammad al-Shaybani al-Jawzaqi told us: Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi told us: Muhammad ibn Hayyuwayh told us: Abu al-Yaman told us: Shu'ayb told us: Abu al-Zinad told us from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayra from him that he said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the weakest in hearts and the softest in feeling. Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni. The head of disbelief is towards the east. Pride and arrogance are among the owners of camels, and arrogance among the owners of horses and camels - the owners of camels are the people of the desert - and tranquility is among the owners of sheep.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Abdullah al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik al-Khallal: Abu al-Qasim Ibrahim ibn Mansur ibn Ibrahim al-Sulami told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn al-Muqri' told us: Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Muthanna al-Mawsili told us: Abu Khaythama told us: Jarir told us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni. The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the softest in hearts and the tenderest in hearts.'

Al-Bukhari and Muslim both narrated it in their Sahihs. Muslim narrated it from Abu Khaythama.

We were informed by Abu Bakr Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirwi in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad al-Tabasi in Nishapur narrated to me from him: al-Qadi Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad al-Hayri told us, and we were informed by Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn told us: Abu Abdullah al-Hafiz told us: both said: Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub told us: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar told us: Abu Mu'awiya told us from al-A'mash from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The people of Yemen have come to you; they are the tenderest in hearts and the softest in feeling. Faith is Yemeni and wisdom is Yemeni.' Al-Hayri added: Abu Mu'awiya said: I think he said: 'The head of disbelief is towards the east.'

We were informed by Sheikh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Muqri' in Baghdad: al-Qadi al-Sharif Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Abd al-Samad ibn al-Muhtadi Billah told us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Shadan al-Sukri al-Harbi told us: Abu Habib al-Abbas ibn Ahmad ibn
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of multiple hadith narrations (with various chains of transmission) from the Prophet Muhammad praising the people of Yemen, specifically the Ash'ari tribe and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The chapter title indicates the subject: 'Chapter on what has been narrated from the Prophet of his glad tidings of the arrival of Abu Musa and the people of Yemen, and his indication of what would appear of the knowledge of Abu al-Hasan' (referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school). Ibn Asakir is gathering these narrations as evidence for the virtue and precedence of the Ash'aris, which is part of his broader defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari against detractors.

The first narration is via Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet announces that a people with softer hearts will come, and when the Ash'aris arrive with Abu Musa, they recite a verse about meeting the beloved (Muhammad). This is repeated through several chains: from Anas via different narrators (Ibn Bukayr, Ibn Abi Adi, Yahya, Yazid, Humayd; via Zuhayr ibn Harb; via Ibn Hamdan). Then it is mentioned that al-Nasa'i also narrated it.

The second set of narrations comes from Abu Hurayra, with multiple chains: the Prophet says the people of Yemen have come, they are the weakest in hearts and softest in feeling, and he emphasizes that faith and wisdom are Yemeni, while the head of disbelief is towards the east, and pride is among camel owners. He also mentions tranquility among sheep owners. This hadith is reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. Then another version from Abu Hurayra via al-A'mash adds that they are the softest and tenderest in hearts.

A third version from Abu Hurayra via Abu Mu'awiya repeats the same content, with an addition that the head of disbelief is towards the east.

Throughout, Ibn Asakir meticulously cites his teachers and chains to authenticate these reports. The purpose is not just to record hadith but to establish a doctrinal point: the Ash'aris (descendants of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari) are divinely praised, and by extension, the theological school attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is rooted in this virtuous lineage. The core argument is that the Prophet's praise serves as a refutation of those who disparage the Ash'ari school.

Key Terms
الإيمان يمان
الحكمة يمانية
رأس الكفر قبل المشرق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet say about the direction of disbelief in the hadith from Abu Hurayra?
A) It is towards the west
B) It is towards the east
C) It is in Yemen
D) It is in the north

Key Takeaway
The hadiths affirm that Yemen is the source of faith and wisdom, thereby honoring the Ash'ari lineage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet described the Yemenis as having soft hearts and tender feelings. When you examine your own heart, do you find it soft and tender towards faith, or has it become hardened by neglect? What one concrete action can you take today to make your heart more receptive to divine guidance?
?
If faith and wisdom are said to be 'Yemeni,' yet you may not be from Yemen, what does your heart rely on to claim true faith? Are you actively seeking wisdom from the same source that produced the Yemeni companions, or are you content with a superficial connection to this religion?
?
The hadith warns that the head of disbelief is towards the east. In your own life, what are the 'eastern' influences – ideas, habits, or companions – that are pulling you away from the simplicity of faith? How can you turn your face towards the 'Yemen' of faith today?

The Prophetic Praise for the Ash'ari People
Hadith narration with chain of transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and identified his people as those whom Allah loves.

Core Idea
The Prophet's gesture linked an entire tribe to divine love.

This lesson examines a key hadith often cited to honor the Ash'ari school. It presents the prophetic tradition that connects the Ash'ari tribe to a Quranic verse promising a beloved community. Pay attention to the chain of narration and the direct gesture of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the chain of narrators from 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz down to 'Iyad al-Ash'ari. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
The chain is long but typical for hadith transmission.
2
Identify the key figures
Notice that the narrator is 'Iyad al-Ash'ari and the Prophet points to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Understand that 'Ash'ari' refers to the tribe, not yet the theological school.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: Why would the Prophet designate a specific tribe as beloved? This sets the stage for later applications to Imam al-Ash'ari.
This connects to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله الحافظ ثنا أبو العباس محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب بن جرير وأبو عامر العقدى قالا ثنا شعبة عن سماك واخبرنا أبو بكر عبدالغفار بن محمد بن الحسين الشيروى فى كتابه وحدثني أبو المحاسن عبد الرزاق بن محمد بن ابي نصر الطبسى بنيسابور عنه قال أنبا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسن الحيرى ثنا محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب عن شعبة قال وثنا ابراهيم ثنا أبو عامر عن شعبة عن سماك بن حرب عن عياض الأشعرى قال لما نزلت (فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) أومأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه فقال (هم قوم هذا) قال البيهقى وذلك لما وجد فيه من الفضيلة الجليلة والرتبة الشريفة للامام ابي الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة باظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة، والأشبه ان يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انما جعل قوم ابى موسى من قوم يحبهم الله ويحبونه، لما علم من صحة دينهم وعرف من قوة يقينهم فمن نحا في علم الأصول نحوهم وتبع فى نفى التشبيه مع ملازمة الكتاب والسنة قولهم جعل من جملتهم وعد من حسابهم بمشيئة الله واذنه اعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده وليعلم المنصف من اصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وامات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق، أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علی بن عبدالله المصرى وأبو بكر ناصر بن ابی العباس بن على الصيدلاني بهراه قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبدالرحمن بن أحمد بن ابی شریح قال نا يحيى بن محمد بن صاعد ثنا أبو سعيد الأشج ثنا عبد الله بن ادريس عن ليث عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل (فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) قال قوم سبا والأشعريون قوم من سبا واكرم بذلك اصلا ونسبا .
Abd Allah al-Hafiz narrated to us from Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi from Shu'bah from Simak; and Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawayh informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi informed me from him from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri from Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb from Shu'bah, and Ibrahim narrated to us from Abu 'Amir from Shu'bah from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When the verse was revealed, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him," the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) and said, "They are the people of this one." Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank that he (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari) possessed. So he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, singled out among them for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is most likely that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made the people of Abu Musa among the people whom Allah loves and who love Him because He knew the soundness of their religion and recognized the strength of their certainty. So whoever pursues the path of the people of Abu Musa in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is counted among them and reckoned with them, by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah help us to that by His grace and seal it with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah in presenting this noble origin, for what He has stored for His servants from this lofty branch through which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us both, saying: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi informed us from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shuraih from Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id from Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj from 'Abd Allah ibn Idris from Layth from Mujahid regarding the saying of Allah Almighty, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him": He said: They are the people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba' — how noble is that origin and lineage!
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a combined narration and commentary. It begins with a hadith narrated by 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: when the Quranic verse "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him" (Quran 5:54) was revealed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said, "They are the people of this one." This establishes a prophetic praise for the Ash'ari tribe. Al-Bayhaqi then comments, applying this praise specifically to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school, because of his great virtue and noble rank. He explains that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is from the people of Abu Musa, meaning he inherits that praise. Bayhaqi then elaborates that among the descendants of Abu Musa, Abu al-Hasan was specially distinguished for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation through clear proofs and refutation of doubts. The passage then gives a reason why the Prophet (peace be upon him) designated the people of Abu Musa: Allah knew the soundness of their faith and the strength of their certainty. Therefore, anyone who follows their path in the science of theological principles (usul) and in negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is considered among them. The passage ends with a separate chain from Mujahid, who interprets the verse as referring to the people of Saba', and notes that the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus linking them to the praised community. The entire section serves to elevate the Ash'ari school by connecting it to prophetic praise and Quranic interpretation.

Key Terms
أبو موسى الأشعري
عياض الأشعري
قوم يحبهم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith refers only to the Ash'ari theological school directly.
Correction: The hadith originally refers to the Ash'ari tribe, specifically Abu Musa's people. The theological school is later linked through interpretation.

Checkpoint
Who did the Prophet point to when the verse about the beloved community was revealed?
A) Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
B) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
C) 'Iyad al-Ash'ari
D) Imam al-Ash'ari

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) explicitly praised the Ash'ari people, designating them as those whom Allah loves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet pointed to a specific tribe as beloved. If you are not from that tribe, what does this hadith teach you about how to become among those whom Allah loves? Use the exact wording of the verse mentioned in the hadith to guide your answer.
?
Reflect on your sincerity: Do you love Allah in a way that would make you eligible to be pointed to? What is one habit you need to change to increase your love for Allah today?

Al-Bayhaqi's Commentary: Imam al-Ash'ari as the Reviver of Sunnah
Al-Bayhaqi's commentary applying hadith to Imam al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bayhaqi's application of the hadith to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, highlighting his role in defending Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
Al-Bayhaqi saw Imam al-Ash'ari as the perfect embodiment of the praised community.

In this commentary, the renowned hadith scholar al-Bayhaqi directly links the prophetic praise to Imam al-Ash'ari, explaining his unique contribution to theology. He emphasizes that Imam al-Ash'ari was specially chosen to strengthen the Sunnah and refute innovations.

Guided Path
1
Read Bayhaqi's commentary
Read the Arabic passage from al-Bayhaqi's statement. Note how he transitions from the hadith to praising Imam al-Ash'ari.
2
Note the specific qualities
Identify the phrases: 'تقوية السنة وقمع البدعة' (strengthening Sunnah, suppressing innovation) and 'باظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة' (manifesting proof, refuting doubts). These define his role.
3
Understand the condition
Bayhaqi states that anyone who follows the path of Abu Musa in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community. This extends the praise to followers of the Ash'ari school.
This is the key theological takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله الحافظ ثنا أبو العباس محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب بن جرير وأبو عامر العقدى قالا ثنا شعبة عن سماك واخبرنا أبو بكر عبدالغفار بن محمد بن الحسين الشيروى فى كتابه وحدثني أبو المحاسن عبد الرزاق بن محمد بن ابي نصر الطبسى بنيسابور عنه قال أنبا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسن الحيرى ثنا محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب عن شعبة قال وثنا ابراهيم ثنا أبو عامر عن شعبة عن سماك بن حرب عن عياض الأشعرى قال لما نزلت (فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) أومأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه فقال (هم قوم هذا) قال البيهقى وذلك لما وجد فيه من الفضيلة الجليلة والرتبة الشريفة للامام ابي الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة باظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة، والأشبه ان يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انما جعل قوم ابى موسى من قوم يحبهم الله ويحبونه، لما علم من صحة دينهم وعرف من قوة يقينهم فمن نحا في علم الأصول نحوهم وتبع فى نفى التشبيه مع ملازمة الكتاب والسنة قولهم جعل من جملتهم وعد من حسابهم بمشيئة الله واذنه اعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده وليعلم المنصف من اصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وامات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق، أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علی بن عبدالله المصرى وأبو بكر ناصر بن ابی العباس بن على الصيدلاني بهراه قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبدالرحمن بن أحمد بن ابی شریح قال نا يحيى بن محمد بن صاعد ثنا أبو سعيد الأشج ثنا عبد الله بن ادريس عن ليث عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل (فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) قال قوم سبا والأشعريون قوم من سبا واكرم بذلك اصلا ونسبا .
Abd Allah al-Hafiz narrated to us from Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi from Shu'bah from Simak; and Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawayh informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi informed me from him from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri from Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb from Shu'bah, and Ibrahim narrated to us from Abu 'Amir from Shu'bah from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When the verse was revealed, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him," the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) and said, "They are the people of this one." Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank that he (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari) possessed. So he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, singled out among them for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is most likely that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made the people of Abu Musa among the people whom Allah loves and who love Him because He knew the soundness of their religion and recognized the strength of their certainty. So whoever pursues the path of the people of Abu Musa in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is counted among them and reckoned with them, by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah help us to that by His grace and seal it with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah in presenting this noble origin, for what He has stored for His servants from this lofty branch through which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us both, saying: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi informed us from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shuraih from Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id from Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj from 'Abd Allah ibn Idris from Layth from Mujahid regarding the saying of Allah Almighty, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him": He said: They are the people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba' — how noble is that origin and lineage!
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a combined narration and commentary. It begins with a hadith narrated by 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: when the Quranic verse "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him" (Quran 5:54) was revealed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said, "They are the people of this one." This establishes a prophetic praise for the Ash'ari tribe. Al-Bayhaqi then comments, applying this praise specifically to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school, because of his great virtue and noble rank. He explains that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is from the people of Abu Musa, meaning he inherits that praise. Bayhaqi then elaborates that among the descendants of Abu Musa, Abu al-Hasan was specially distinguished for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation through clear proofs and refutation of doubts. The passage then gives a reason why the Prophet (peace be upon him) designated the people of Abu Musa: Allah knew the soundness of their faith and the strength of their certainty. Therefore, anyone who follows their path in the science of theological principles (usul) and in negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is considered among them. The passage ends with a separate chain from Mujahid, who interprets the verse as referring to the people of Saba', and notes that the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus linking them to the praised community. The entire section serves to elevate the Ash'ari school by connecting it to prophetic praise and Quranic interpretation.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
نفي التشبيه
أصول
السنة
البدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what was Imam al-Ash'ari's special role among the descendants of Abu Musa?
A) He was the most knowledgeable in jurisprudence
B) He was singled out for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts
C) He was the wealthiest scholar of his time
D) He was the only one who memorized the Quran

Key Takeaway
Al-Bayhaqi shows that anyone who follows the Ash'ari path in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you someone who loves the People of the Sunnah because of their adherence to the Book and Sunnah, or do you find yourself critical of them? Are you willing to examine your heart and see if you truly love those whom Allah loves?
?
Bayhaqi says that anyone who follows the Ash'ari path in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community. If you claim to follow this path, do your daily actions and intellectual pursuits reflect a genuine defense of the Sunnah and rejection of innovation, or is it just a label?
?
The Prophet praised the people of Abu Musa for their sound religion and strong certainty. How certain are you in your own beliefs? Are you willing to devote effort to strengthen your faith through study of usul, or do you remain passive?

The Ash'ari Lineage: From Saba' to Prophetic Praise
Narration from Mujahid linking the verse to Saba' and Ash'aris

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the connection between the Ash'aris, the people of Saba', and the Quranic verse, as narrated from the early scholar Mujahid.

Core Idea
The Ash'aris trace their blessed lineage back to Saba', a people mentioned in the Quran.

This lesson presents a separate interpretation from the early scholar Mujahid, who identifies the beloved community in the verse as the people of Saba', and notes that the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus reinforcing their honored status from a different angle.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration from Mujahid
Read the Arabic chain and the statement of Mujahid. Note that he interprets 'people whom Allah loves' as the people of Saba'.
This is a tafsir narration.
2
Reflect on the dual honor
The Ash'aris are not only praised by the Prophet but also linked to a Quranically honored people (Saba'). This adds a layer of prestige.

Hadith of the Renewer Every Hundred Years and Early Mujaddids
Hadith and identification of first two mujaddids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith promising a renewer every century and the early scholarly identification of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the first two mujaddids.

Core Idea
Allah sends a renewer for this ummah every century.

This lesson presents a key hadith that promises religious renewal at the start of each century. We will read the hadith as transmitted by Abu Dawud and others, and see how early scholars identified the first two renewers: 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the Arabic hadith carefully, noting its promise that Allah will send a renewer every hundred years.
The hadith is attributed to Abu Hurayrah and is considered authentic.
2
Understand 'renewal of religion'
Reflect on what 'tajdid al-din' means: reviving and purifying the faith, not introducing new doctrines.
3
Identify the first two mujaddids
Note the early authorities' identification: 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz for the first century and Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i for the second.
These identifications are based on the hadith and scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اخبرنا الشيخان أبو القسم عبدالملك بن عبد الله بن داود المغربي وأبو غالب محمد بن الحسن بن على البصرى الماوردى ببغداد قالا أنبا أبو على على بن أحمد بن على التسترى بالبصرة ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو عمر أحمد بن القسم بن جعفر بن عبد الواحد الهاشمي، ثنا أبو على محمد بن عمرو اللؤلؤى ثنا أبو داود سليمان بن الاشعث السجستاني في كتاب السنن قال ثنا سليمان بن داود المهرى أنبا ابن وهب اخبرنی سعید بن ابی ايوب عن شراحيل بن يزيد المعافري عن ابي علقمة عن ابي هريرة فيما أعلم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( ان الله عز وجل يبعث لهذه الأمة على رأس كل مائة سنة من يجدد لها دينها قال أبو داود رواه الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن شريح الاسكندرانى لم يخبر به شراحيل اخبرناه الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندى انا أبو القسم اسماعيل بن مسعدة الجرجاني ببغداد انا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى انا أبو أحمد عبد الله بن عدى الجرجانى انا العباس بن محمد بن العباس البصري والقسم بن عبد الله بن مهدی نا حميم قالا نا عمرو بن سواد السرحي ح قال أبو أحمد بن عدى ونا يحيى بن محمد بن يحيى بن اخي حرملة بن یحيى نا عمى حرملة بن يحيى ح قال أبو أحمد وانا محمد بن هرون بن حسان ومحمد بن علی بن الحسين قالا نا أحمد بن عبدالرحمن بن وهب قالوا ثنا ابن وهب قال حدثني سعيد بن أبى ايوب عن شراحيل بن يزيد المعافري عن أبي علقمة عن ابي هريرة فيما أعلم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( ان الله يبعث لهذه الأمة على رأس كل مائة سنة من يجدد لها دينها ) . قال محمد بن علی بن الحسين سمعت أصحابنا يقولون كان في المائة الأولى عمر بن عبد العزيز وفى المائة الثانية محمد بن ادريس الشافعي رحمة عليهما
The two shaykhs, Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Dawud al-Maghribi and Abu Ghalib Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Basri al-Mawardi in Baghdad, informed us both, saying: Abu 'Ali 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Tustari in Basra informed us from the noble judge Abu 'Umar Ahmad ibn al-Qasim ibn Ja'far ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Hashimi from Abu 'Ali Muhammad ibn 'Amr al-Lu'lu'i from Abu Dawud Sulayman ibn al-Ash'ath al-Sijistani in the Book of Sunan from Sulayman ibn Dawud al-Mahri from Ibn Wahb from Sa'id ibn Abi Ayyub from Sharahil ibn Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqamah from Abu Hurayrah — as far as I know — from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: "Indeed, Allah Almighty will send for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew for it its religion." Abu Dawud said: It was narrated by Shaykh 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Shuraih al-Iskandarani but he did not report it from Sharahil. It was narrated to us by Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi from Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'adah al-Jurjani in Baghdad from Abu al-Qasim Hamzah ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi from Abu Ahmad 'Abd Allah ibn 'Adi al-Jurjani from al-'Abbas ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Basri and al-Qasim ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Mahdi from Humaym from 'Amr ibn Sawwad al-Sarhi; and Abu Ahmad ibn 'Adi narrated to us from Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Akhi Harmalah ibn Yahya from my uncle Harmalah ibn Yahya; and Abu Ahmad narrated to us from Muhammad ibn Harun ibn Hassan and Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn from Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Wahb from Ibn Wahb from Sa'id ibn Abi Ayyub from Sharahil ibn Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqamah from Abu Hurayrah — as far as I know — from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: "Indeed, Allah sends for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew for it its religion." Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn said: I heard our companions say: In the first century it was 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, and in the second century it was Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i — may Allah have mercy on them both.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a hadith report with multiple chains of transmission, followed by an identification of the early renewers. The primary hadith, from Abu Hurayrah, states that Allah sends for the Muslim community (ummah) at the beginning of every hundred years someone who will renew (yujaddid) the religion. The text includes two parallel chains via Abu Dawud and others to establish the hadith's authenticity. After the hadith, the narrator Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn (likely the son of Imam al-Husayn) reports that the early authorities (aṣḥābinā) identified the first-century renewer as 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz (the Umayyad caliph known for his piety and reforms) and the second-century renewer as Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i (the founder of the Shafi'i school of law). This passage thus provides both the textual basis for the concept of tajdid (renewal) and early examples of who fulfilled that role. The multiple chains emphasize the reliability of the hadith, while the identification shows how early scholars understood and applied the prophecy.

عمر بن عبد العزيز
محمد بن إدريس الشافعي
رأس كل مائة سنة
أبو داود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means exactly one renewer is sent every century and no more.
Correction: The hadith is a general promise that renewal will occur, not that there is only one renewer per century or that every century has a single identifiable figure.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who were identified as the renewers (mujaddids) for the first and second centuries?
A) Abu Bakr and 'Umar
B) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i
C) Abu Hanifah and Malik ibn Anas
D) Ahmad ibn Hanbal and al-Ash'ari

Key Takeaway
The hadith promises renewal every century, and early scholars identified 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the first two renewers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to rely on the scholars of the past, or are you actively seeking to be part of the ongoing renewal of this religion? What is one action you can take today to embody the spirit of tajdid?
?
If Allah sent a renewer in every century, what does that imply about your own responsibility to learn and revive your faith? Will you wait for others or take the first step yourself?

Imam Ahmad's Praise for al-Shafi'i and the Hadith on Qurayshi Scholars
Ibn 'Asakir quotes Imam Ahmad deferring to al-Shafi'i and a hadith about a scholar from Quraysh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context and significance of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's deference to Imam al-Shafi'i and the prophetic hadith about a Qurayshi scholar.

Core Idea
Imam Ahmad relied on al-Shafi'i when lacking textual evidence, because he was a Qurayshi scholar whose knowledge would fill the earth.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work provides a fascinating glimpse into the relationship between two of the greatest early Sunni imams: Ahmad ibn Hanbal and al-Shafi'i. It shows Ahmad's profound respect for al-Shafi'i's scholarship, even as an imam of his own school. The lesson will examine the report, the hadith cited, and the implications for understanding how early scholars viewed authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Note the chain of transmission and the core statement.
The text ends abruptly; focus on the part we have.
2
Identify the chain of transmission
Trace the isnad from al-Marwarrudhi back to the Prophet (SAW) for the hadith. Notice the sequence of narrators.
This shows the care early scholars took in preserving reports.
3
Analyze Ahmad's statement
What did Ahmad say he does when faced with a question for which he knows no 'khabar'? Why does he rely on al-Shafi'i?
Ahmad's reason is that al-Shafi'i is a Qurayshi imam.
4
Connect to the hadith
How does the hadith about a Qurayshi scholar support Ahmad's deference? Discuss the link between the hadith and al-Shafi'i.
The hadith is a promise that a Qurayshi scholar will spread knowledge.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
Some think Ahmad always followed al-Shafi'i. Read the statement again: it's specifically when he lacks textual evidence.
This humility reflects the methodology of early imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اخبرنا الشيخ أبو المعالي محمد بن اسماعيل بن محمد بن الحسين الفارسي بنيسابور انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن على البيهقى انا أبو عبدالرحمن محمد بن الحسين السلمى نا أبو عبد الله محمد بن العباس العصمى نا أبو اسحق أحمد بن محمد بن ياسين الهروي قال سمعت ابراهيم بن اسحاق الانصارى يقول سمعت المروروذی صاحب احمد بن حنبل يقول قال احمد : إذا سألت عن مسألة لا أعلم فيها خبرا قلت فيها يقول الشافعي لانه امام عالم من قریش وروى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انه قال ( عالم قريش يملأ الأرض علما وذكر في الخبر ان الله يقيض عليه
The shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Farisi in Nishapur informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali al-Bayhaqi narrated to us from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Sulami from Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-'Asmi from Abu Ishaq Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Yasin al-Harawi who said: I heard Ibrahim ibn Ishaq al-Ansari say: I heard al-Marwarrudhi, the companion of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, say: Ahmad said: When I am asked about a matter for which I know no report (khabar), I say in it: 'Al-Shafi'i says such-and-such,' because he is an imam, a scholar from Quraysh. And it was narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'A scholar from Quraysh will fill the earth with knowledge.' And it is mentioned in the report that Allah will appoint...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a biographical report about Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's high regard for Imam al-Shafi'i. It is transmitted through a chain leading to al-Marwarrudhi, a companion of Ahmad. Ahmad states that when he is asked about a legal issue for which he knows no explicit textual evidence (khabar), he relies on the opinion of al-Shafi'i, saying 'Al-Shafi'i says such-and-such.' The reason he gives is that al-Shafi'i is an imam, a scholar from Quraysh. This indicates that Ahmad considered al-Shafi'i to be a source of authority in matters of law, especially when direct scriptural evidence was lacking. Then Ahmad references a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that 'a scholar from Quraysh will fill the earth with knowledge,' implying that al-Shafi'i is that scholar. The passage ends abruptly with 'and it is mentioned in the report that Allah will appoint...' (likely referring to the continuation of the hadith or another tradition). This passage demonstrates the mutual respect among early Sunni imams and specifically elevates al-Shafi'i as a renewer of knowledge.

عالم قريش

قریش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam Ahmad always followed al-Shafi'i's opinions.
Correction: Ahmad only relied on al-Shafi'i when he had no explicit textual report on the matter, not as a general rule.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam Ahmad's reliance on al-Shafi'i for issues where he lacked direct evidence highlights the humility and mutual respect among early imams, and ties to a prophetic promise about a Qurayshi scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Hadith of the Renewer and Its Early Interpretation
Narrates the renewer hadith via two chains and identifies Umar and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wording and dual transmission of the renewer hadith, and the early scholarly identification of Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the renewers of the first two centuries.

Core Idea
The renewer hadith promises a reviver of religion every century, with early scholars identifying Umar and Shafi'i.

This lesson presents the famous hadith about the renewer (mujaddid) as transmitted through two chains from Abu Hurayra. It also records an early application where companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and Muhammad bin Idris al-Shafi'i. Understanding this hadith and its early interpretation helps us appreciate the concept of renewal in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its two chains
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the hadith is transmitted through two separate chains, both ending with Abu Hurayra. The second chain includes an additional identification of the renewers.
The first chain is via Abu Dawud, the second via Ibn Wahb and others.
2
Identify the promise and its timing
The hadith states that Allah will raise for this community at the head of every hundred years someone who renews its religion. Note the phrase 'on the head of every hundred years' meaning at the beginning of each century.
3
Observe the early application
After the second chain, the narrator Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn reports that his companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz for the first century and al-Shafi'i for the second.
This is an early example of applying the hadith to specific historical figures.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i were chosen. Consider their contributions to Islamic scholarship and revival. Also note that the hadith does not name individuals; the identification is interpretive.
This connects to the common misunderstanding that the hadith specifies particular individuals.

Ahmad bin al-Qasim bin Ja'far bin Abd al-Wahid al-Hashimi narrated to us: Abu Ali Muhammad bin Amr al-Lu'lu'i narrated to us, Abu Dawud Sulayman bin al-Ash'ath al-Sijistani narrated to us in the book of Sunan, he said: Sulayman bin Dawud al-Mahri narrated to us, Ibn Wahb informed us, Sa'id bin Abi Ayyub informed me from Shirahil bin Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqama from Abu Hurayra, as far as I know, from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, will raise for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew its religion for it.' Abu Dawud said: The Shaykh Abd al-Rahman bin Shurayh al-Iskandarani narrated it, he did not inform Shirahil of it. We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il bin Ahmad al-Samarqandi, we were informed by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il bin Mas'ada al-Jurjani in Baghdad, we were informed by Abu al-Qasim Hamza bin Yusuf al-Sahmi, we were informed by Abu Ahmad Abd Allah bin Adi al-Jurjani, we were informed by al-Abbas bin Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Basri and al-Qasim bin Abd Allah bin Mahdi, they said: Humaym narrated to us, they said: Amr bin Sawad al-Sarhi narrated to us. Abu Ahmad bin Adi said: And Yahya bin Muhammad bin Yahya, the nephew of Harmala bin Yahya, narrated to us, they said: Harmala bin Yahya narrated to us. Abu Ahmad said: And Muhammad bin Harun bin Hassan and Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn narrated to us, they said: Ahmad bin Abd al-Rahman bin Wahb narrated to us, they said: Ibn Wahb narrated to us, he said: Sa'id bin Abi Ayyub narrated to me from Shirahil bin Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqama from Abu Hurayra, as far as I know, from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Indeed Allah raises for this community at the head of every hundred years one who renews its religion for it.' Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn said: I heard our companions saying: In the first century it was Umar bin Abd al-Aziz, and in the second century it was Muhammad bin Idris al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a dual transmission of the famous hadith about the renewer (mujaddid). It presents two chains: one via Abu Dawud and another via Ibn Wahb, both from Abu Hurayra with the same wording. After the second chain, the narrator Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn reports that his companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz for the first century and Imam al-Shafi'i for the second. This establishes an early precedent for applying the hadith to specific scholars, linking the concept of renewal to key figures in Islamic history.

Misconception: The hadith names specific individuals as renewers for each century.
Correction: The hadith is a generic promise that Allah will raise a renewer; the identification of Umar and Shafi'i is an interpretive application by early scholars, not a direct statement of the hadith.

Ahmad ibn Hanbal on al-Shafi'i and the Renewer
Ahmad ibn Hanbal praises al-Shafi'i and identifies him as the second renewer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahmad ibn Hanbal viewed al-Shafi'i as an authoritative source and connected him to the prophetic tradition of religious renewal.

Core Idea
Ahmad ibn Hanbal relied on al-Shafi'i as a Quraysh scholar and renewer.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work preserves a remarkable statement from Ahmad ibn Hanbal showing his deep respect for al-Shafi'i. Ahmad explains that when he lacks direct textual evidence, he turns to al-Shafi'i's opinion because of his lineage and knowledge. He then links al-Shafi'i to the famous hadith about a renewer every century, identifying him as the renewer of the second Islamic century. This lesson explores the significance of these claims and what they reveal about early scholarly relationships.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the key statements from Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
The isnad shows this information was transmitted through reliable scholars like al-Bayhaqi.
2
Understand Ahmad's practice
Ahmad says he quotes al-Shafi'i when he doesn't know a report. Ask: Why does he choose al-Shafi'i specifically? What does this tell us about Ahmad's methodology?
Ahmad does not follow al-Shafi'i blindly; he acknowledges his authority in certain cases.
3
Connect to the renewer tradition
Ahmad cites the hadith about a renewer every hundred years and explicitly names Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i as the first two renewers. Reflect on the implications for al-Shafi'i's status.
This shows that early scholars saw renewal as a continuous process.
4
Note the supplication for al-Shafi'i
The narrator Abu Abd Allah says he has been praying for al-Shafi'i in his prayers for forty years. Consider what this demonstrates about personal devotion and respect.
This indicates that al-Shafi'i was held in high esteem even by later scholars.

We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad bin Isma'il bin Muhammad bin al-Husayn al-Farisi in Nishapur: Abu Bakr Ahmad bin al-Husayn bin Ali al-Bayhaqi informed us: Abu Abd al-Rahman Muhammad bin al-Husayn al-Sulami informed us: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Asami narrated to us: Abu Ishaq Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Yasin al-Harawi narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibrahim bin Ishaq al-Ansari say: I heard al-Marwadhi, the companion of Ahmad bin Hanbal, say: Ahmad said: 'If I am asked about a matter for which I know no report, I say in it: al-Shafi'i says, because he is an imam from Quraysh.' The passage demonstrates the high esteem later scholars held for al-Shafi'i and connects him to the renewal tradition.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Three Revivers of Religion: Ahmad, Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aim
Report of al-Sa'luki crediting three scholars with reviving religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the report crediting three scholars—Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi—with reviving Islam after it had largely disappeared.

Core Idea
Allah revived religion through three scholars: Ahmad, Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aim.

This lesson presents a concise yet powerful report from the renowned scholar Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki (with a note of narrator uncertainty). It identifies three figures who, according to al-Sa'luki, were instruments of Allah in restoring the religion after a period of decline. As you read, note the chain of transmission and the precise wording, which highlights the collaborative role of these scholars in reviving Islamic knowledge and practice.

Guided Path
1
Examine the transmission chain
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the chain from the author through al-Qumisi, al-Sahlaki, and al-Razjahi, with the narrator's uncertainty about whether the speaker was al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili. This shows the care in preserving reports.
The uncertainty is captured by the phrase 'أو الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر الإسمعيلي' and 'والشك مني'.
2
Identify the three scholars named
Find the names: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi. Reflect on their fields: hadith/fiqh, theology, and spirituality.
Each scholar contributed uniquely to the revival of Sunnism.
3
Understand the meaning of 'reviving religion'
The phrase 'بعد ما ذهب' suggests a period when the religion had largely disappeared. The revival means restoring its teachings and practices.
This is not about physical revival but renewal of knowledge and adherence.
4
Consider the narrator's doubt
The transmitter is unsure whether the saying came from al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili. This does not affect the content but reminds us of the human element in transmission.
Such doubts are common in hadith and historical reports.

اخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر أحمد بن الحسين القومسى بها انا جدى لأمى أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد السهلكي قال حكى الفقيه الصالح الثقة أبو عمرو یعنی محمد بن عبدالله الأديب الرزجاهى قال سمعت الاستاذ الامام ابا سهل الصعلوكي ام الشيخ الامام ابا بكر الاسمعيلى ذكر واحدا والشك منى يقول : اعاد الله تعالى هذا الدين بعد ماذهب يعنى اكثره بأحمد بن حنبل وابي الحسن الأشعري وابي نعيم الاسترابادى
We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Ahmad bin al-Husayn al-Qumisi there: my maternal grandfather Abu al-Fadl Muhammad bin Ali bin Ahmad al-Sahlaki informed us, he said: The righteous and trustworthy jurist Abu Amr, meaning Muhammad bin Abd Allah al-Adib al-Razjahi, related: I heard the teacher and imam Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki, or the shaykh and imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili? — he mentioned one, and I am uncertain — say: 'Allah, Exalted, restored this religion after it had gone, meaning most of it, through Ahmad bin Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi.'
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a report from al-Sa'luki (with a note of uncertainty from the transmitter about whether it was al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili) stating that Allah revived the religion after it had largely disappeared through three scholars: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi. This presents a broader view of renewal involving multiple figures across different fields: hadith and fiqh (Ahmad), theology and defense of Sunnism (Ash'ari), and perhaps hadith or Sufism (Abu Nu'aim). The phrasing 'after it had gone' suggests a period of decline followed by revival through these scholars' efforts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If Allah revives religion through scholars, what are you doing to ensure you are not part of a generation that lets the religion 'go' again? What personal accountability do you feel for the preservation of true Islam?
